Formulas such as Chuanxiong San, Shen Yu San, as well as Ma Huang, Zi Su, Jing Jie, and green onion can be chosen for use.

    2. If the nasal obstruction is due to upward-ascending fire evil, it is necessary to clear the fire. When the fire is mild, it is often closer to the upper jiao, arising from the heart and lungs. One should use clearing and transforming drinks like Huangqin Zhi Mu Decoction. If the fire is severe, it usually stems from the Yangming stage and may be accompanied by a slight headache. In such cases, Bamboo Leaf and Gypsum Decoction or Liangge San can be employed.

    In cases of concurrent wind-cold and fire, one may also use formulas like Fangfeng Tongsheng San. Generally, persistent nasal obstruction is more related to fire, while sudden blockage is more often due to wind-cold; it is important to differentiate between the two.

    Excess nasal discharge is often attributed to fire; thus, it is said that with severe lung heat, nasal discharge increases. From this perspective, excessive tearing or salivation without cause also indicates heat in the liver and spleen, as they belong to the same category.

    The condition of nasal dripping is mainly due to the fire in the Taiyang and Du meridians; when severe, it connects to the brain, leading to continuous discharge, hence also known as "brain leakage." This condition often arises from indulgence in alcohol, excessive fatty and sweet foods, prolonged use of hot substances, or fire being constrained by cold, resulting in damp-heat rising and causing fluids to overflow and degrade, with some discharges being foul-smelling and quite unbearable. In such cases, in the Hejian area, one may use Fangfeng Tongsheng San with an addition of peppermint and Huanglian, each two qian for treatment. Historically, Cang Er San has also been used for this condition.[50p]
    However, in my view, this fire rising in heat affects both the treatment of accompanying dryness and dispersing methods, leading to unsatisfactory results. It is better to simply clear the Yang fire while also nourishing the Yin; over time, this will bring tranquility. This is the method of suppressing the excessive. Therefore, one often adds five qian or one liang of white tribulus and two or three qian of cicada shells to a cleansing beverage. If the heat is severe, one can further adjust the dosage of cooling agents to effectively achieve complete recovery. Alternatively, using a decoction like Xuanming Fangfeng Tang is also acceptable. However, once this condition occurs, it is essential to regulate and treat it early; if left untreated for a long time, it becomes very difficult to remedy.

    In cases of nasal or cerebral discharge, although they may be heat symptoms, if the discharge has persisted for a long time, the fire pathogen is already gone, but the discharge continues because the pathway is unable to seal properly. Therefore, new cases are often due to heat, while chronic cases may not necessarily all be heat symptoms. This must be carefully assessed in treatment; if one insists on using cold and cooling methods, it may inadvertently lead to the development of other illnesses.[51p]
    If there is excessive leakage, harming the marrow sea, then the qi becomes deficient above, leading to symptoms such as headaches and dizziness. This requires the supplementation of yang, and can be treated with formulas like Sheng Qi Tang or Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang.

    Nasal polyps block the nasal passages; although the nose is an orifice of the lungs, this blockage in the patient is a disease of the meridians and muscles. This is actually due to the retention and stagnation of heat in the Yangming channel. Therefore, the internal treatment should focus on clearing fire and qi, while external treatment should utilize Huang Bai San, Qian Jin Polyp Decoction, Xiong Huang San, or simpler formulas for polyps.

    For a red nose caused by excessive drinking, this often occurs in individuals who enjoy alcohol, leading to damp-heat invading and steaming the lungs, resulting in blood heat. Alternatively, some might develop red and black lesions from wind-heat in the lung channel. Internally, it is advisable to cool the blood and clear the fire; externally, one should use sulfur powder or alum powder for gentle application.[52p]
    Secret Records of the Stone Chamber 【Qing Dynasty, Chen Shiduo】

    Swelling and Pain Caused by Fire

    When the nose is swollen, it indicates excess fire in the lung meridian and is best treated with a sweet tangerine decoction. Now, if powdered soapberry is blown into the nose, and one sneezes numerous times, relief will be achieved. This is because the congestion in the nose will be released when one sneezes, allowing the obstructed energy to disperse, hence there is no need to clear the lungs for the nasal swelling to subside.

    Large Nose

    There are people whose noses are large like a fist, causing unbearable pain. This is due to the fire heat in the lung meridian being blocked in the nose and unable to discharge. The method is to clear the evil from the lungs and remove the fire in the nose. The prescription uses three qian (a unit of weight) each of Huangqin (Scutellaria), Maidong (Ophiopogon), flower pollen, and licorice; five qian each of Jiegang (Platycodon) and Tiandong (Asparagus); two qian of Zihuan (Aster); and one qian each of Baibu (Stemona) and Suye (Perilla leaf), decocted in water for consumption; four doses will resolve the issue. This formula mainly focuses on clearing the lung meridian to eliminate its fiery evil, which is why the swelling and blockage will not persist. This is a peculiar illness treated with conventional methods.[53p]
    Kong Sheng's Red Line

    A red line grows in the nose, about a foot long; if it moves even slightly, it causes excruciating pain. People believe it to be a condition caused by drinking alcohol, but I think otherwise; it is also a form of haunting. I used a mixture of borax and borneol, each one part, ground into powder, then mixed with human milk and gently applied to the middle of the red line. Suddenly, it felt as if someone had punched the patient, and in an instant, it disappeared. This is an extraordinary remedy. Borax is also known for its ability to dispel hauntings.

    Nasal Gate

    Formula

    Li Ze Tong Qi Decoction (from "Standard" below): for treating nasal congestion.
    Each of the following: Chuanxiong, Du Hou, Fang Feng (remove the fork), Sheng Ma, Ge Gen, 8 parts; Chuan Jiao and Ma Huang (with stems), 4 parts; in winter add 1.2 parts of Cang Zhu; 1.6 parts each of Bai Zhi and Huang Qi; 0.8 parts of Gan Cao. Prepare as one dose, with 2 cups of water, 3 slices of ginger, 2 jujubes, and 3 inches of scallion white, boil down to 1 cup, strain, and take warm away from food. Avoid all cold items and sitting or lying in drafty or cool places.

    Wen Fei Decoction: for the above symptoms.
    1.0 parts each of Sheng Ma, Huang Qi, Ding Xiang, Ge Gen, Qiang Huo, and Gan Cao (raw); 4 parts of Ma Huang (without stems). Grind coarsely, divide into two doses, each with 2 large cups of water, 2 stalks of scallion white, boil down to 1 cup, strain, and take warm away from food.[54p]
    Cold-Resistant Soup: Treats cold air. Wind evil affects the skin, leading to nasal congestion, cough, and wheezing. Ingredients: 1 qian Huangqi, 5 fen each of Ren Shen, Sheng Ma, Chen Pi; 3 fen each of Gan Cao, Donghua, Fo Er Cao, Fang Feng; 3 fen each of Huang Lian, Huang Bo, Qiang Huo, Bai Zhi; 7 fen Cang Zhu; 2 large bowls of water, boil down to 1 bowl, strain, warm slightly, take before meals.

    Warm Defense Soup: Treats previous symptoms. Ingredients: 1 qian Sheng Huangqi, Cang Zhu, Sheng Ma, Zhi Mu, Qiang Huo, Chai Hu, Dang Gui each; 5 fen each of Ren Shen, Huang Bo, Bai Zhi, Fang Feng, Gan Cao (roasted), Ze Xie; 3 fen each of Chen Pi, Qing Pi, Mu Xiang, Huang Lian; 2 bowls of water, boil down to 1 bowl, strain, take warm before meals on sunny days.

    Warm Defense Blood Supplement Soup: Treats previous symptoms. Ingredients: 1 qian 2 fen Huangqi, 4 fen Sheng Ma; 3 fen each of Chai Hu, roasted Gan Cao, fresh Gan Cao, Di Gu Pi, Jie Geng, Ren Shen; 1 fen each of Bai Zhu, Sheng Di Huang, Huo Xiang, Wu Zhu Yu, Huang Bo; 2 fen each of Cang Zhu, Chen Pi, Wang Gua Gen, Mu Dan Pi; 3 pieces of Tao Ren; 2.5 fen Dang Gui; 7 blossoms of Kui Hua; 1 clove of Ding Xiang; 2 bowls of water, boil down to 1.5 bowls, strain, warm slightly, take before meals.[55p]
    Ginseng Decoction: Treats lung qi ascending, causing nasal congestion.
    Ginseng, white poria, Huang Qin (Scutellaria), aged tangerine peel (white part removed), Qiang Huo, Ephedra (roots and joints removed), Sichuan pepper (eyes and/or mouth removed), stir-fry until sweat appears, each half a qian. Use two sheng of water, decoct until one sheng remains, take after meals.

    Magnolia Flower Powder: Treats lung deficiency affected by the four qi, causing nasal obstruction and continuous discharge. Sometimes breath becomes obstructed, cannot smell scents or odors.
    Magnolia flower, Chuanxiong, Mutong (joints removed), Xinxiang (washed clean of soil), Qiang Huo, Fang Feng, dried root of Kudzu, Sheng Ma, Bai Zhi, roasted licorice, each an equal portion. Cang Er Zi (reduce by half), grind into a fine powder, take two qian after meals with clear tea.

    Increased and Decreased Tongshengtang Powder: Treats disharmony of lung qi, causing nasal obstruction and difficulty.
    Rat sticky seed, Platycodon, white mulberry bark, and Ziwans, each one and a half qian; Jing Jie (two qian), fresh licorice (seven fen). Use two sheng of water, three slices of ginger, decoct to one sheng, take after meals.

    Magnolia Flower Decoction: Treats unfavorable lung qi, dizziness, heavy nasal obstruction, and thick phlegm.
    Magnolia flower (hair removed), Chuanxiong, Bai Zhi, sweet chrysanthemum flowers, Sheng Di Huang, gypsum, Bai Zhu, Qian Hu, mint leaves, red poria (skin removed), old tangerine peel (white part removed), each one liang; roasted licorice two liang. Mix thoroughly, take five qian after meals with one and a half sheng of water, decoct to one sheng, remove dregs, take warm away from meals.[56p]
    Da Hu San: Treats colds, nasal congestion, and a heavy voice.
    Ingredients: Half a tael of xixin, one tael of chuangxiong, one and a half taels of mint, one tael of prepared chuanwu (peeled and spliced), two taels each of bai zhi and licorice. Grind the above into a fine powder. Dosage: One qian, mixed with scallion tea or mint soup for consumption.

    Tongguan San: Treats nasal wind with blockage, inability to smell; may also include clear nasal discharge, frequent sneezing, tightness in the shoulders and neck, and headaches.
    Ingredients: Original silkworm moth (baked until yellow), prepared white fuzi, peeled yizhi, mint, fried tribulus (without corners), and bitter gentian, each half a tael. Grind the above into a fine powder. Dosage: Three qian, taken with warm wine at any time.

    Fangfeng Soup ("Xuanming"): Treats nasal congestion with persistent clear nasal discharge.
    Ingredients: Half a tael each of fangfeng and guan gui, seven pieces of zhi zi, one tael of sheng ma, three taels of ground gypsum, and seven and a half qian of ma huang, one tael and two and a half qian of mu tong. Crush the above into pieces. Dosage: Three qian, boiled with one cup of water, reduce to two thirds, discard the dregs, and take it warm on an empty stomach, twice daily.

    Pai Feng San: Treats nasal congestion and may also treat growths like polyps.
    Ingredients: Half a tael of fangfeng, qin jiao (with soil and sprouts removed), wu zhu yu (soaked in soup and baked), one tael each of yam and tian xiong (peeled and spliced), half a tael of qiang huo. Grind into fine powder. Dosage: Two qian, taken with warm wine on an empty stomach.[57p]

    Treats nasal congestion.
    Ingredients: 1.5 taels of Bitter Orange, 3 qian of mint leaves, 2.5 qian of schizonepeta spikes. Grind together into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of cherries. Dissolve one or two pills as needed.

    Treats nasal blockages causing difficulty breathing.
    Ingredients: Equal parts acorus and soapberry. Grind into a powder; each use 1 qian, wrap in cotton and plug into the nose, lying on your back for a short time.

    Treats nasal congestion.
    Ingredients: 2.5 qian each of huanglian (yellow gentian) and talc, 7 pieces of claw stem. Grind thoroughly, use a small amount to blow into the nose for immediate relief.

    Treats nasal congestion.
    Ingredients: 1 tael each of chuanxiong and magnolia flower, 7.5 qian of asarum without soil, 0.5 tael of mutong (clematis). Grind into a fine powder; each use a small amount wrapped in cotton to plug the nose. Change it when damp; typically heals in 5 to 7 days.

    Claw Stem Powder
    Treats nasal congestion.
    Ingredients: Equal parts gourd stem and rhizoma. Grind into powder; each use 1 qian, wrap in cotton and plug into the nose, change twice daily.

    Chuanxiong Powder
    Treats nasal ulcers.
    Ingredients: 1 fen each of chuanxiong, cinnamon, asarum, betel nut, ephedra (without nodes), fangji (stephania), mutong, stone acorus, and white atractylodes; 0.5 fen each of wood fragrance and Sichuan pepper, and half a fen of honeyed licorice. Chew together; each serving 3 qian, with 2 cups of water, 3 slices of ginger, and a small amount of perilla leaves. Simmer until reduced to 80%, strain, and take warm away from food.[58p]
    Shan Zhuyu Pill: Treats nasal issues.

    Ingredients:

    • Shan Zhuyu, Dahuang (prepared), and Chrysanthemum flowers (stems and leaves removed) each 2.5 taels
    • Shi Buxiao (xiao) 3.75 taels
    • Fuzi (prepared, skin and navel removed) 7.5 qian
    • Duhuo 7.5 qian
    • Qin Jiao (stems and soil removed) 1.5 taels
    • Mianjingzi (white skin removed)
    • Zhi Mu (skin removed and prepared)
    • Fangfeng and roasted Licorice each 1 tael

    Grind into a fine powder and mix with honey to form pills the size of a tung seed. Take 30 pills on an empty stomach, sending them down with warm wine. Suitable for the elderly. If pregnant, omit Fuzi and add half a fen of Xixin.

    Chilong Powder: Generally addresses lung issues that manifest in the nose, affecting the head and face. If there is stagnation in the upper body and wind-cold obstructs the head, the qi is not able to flow; cold air accumulates and blocks the fluids, resulting in congestion and nasal issues, causing the inability to smell.

    Ingredients:

    • Longao 0.5 qian, ground
    • Gua Ti, ground, 14 pieces
    • Chixiaodou 30 grains
    • Huanglian 3 large stems

    Grind into a fine powder and mix thoroughly. Use a small amount of this mixture and blow it into the nostrils before sleeping, leading to drainage and recovery.

    • Zaojiao meat 0.5 fen

    Xionghuang Powder for treating nasal issues.
    0.5 qian of xionghuang, 2 pieces of gourd stems, 1 qian of green vitriol, a small amount of musk. Grind together into a fine powder. Use a small amount (oral) in the nostrils; it also treats nasal polyps.

    Huangbai Powder for treating nasal issues, polyps, nasal hemorrhoids, etc.
    0.5 qian of xionghuang, 1 qian each of white vitriol, gourd stems, and asarum. Grind into a fine powder, mix with the bile of a male dog, form into pills, and pack in cotton to block the nose. Another method is to use the powder (oral) in the nostrils.

    Tongcao Powder for treating nasal issues, difficulty breathing, inability to smell, and nasal polyps.
    Equal parts of tongcao, asarum, and aconite. Grind into a fine powder, mix with honey, and pack a small amount into the nostrils.

    Chuanjiao Powder for treating nasal discharge.
    Chuanjiao to open the mouth, stir-fried to sweat, remove the pit of the haritaki fruit, spicy cinnamon, chuanxiong, raw ginger, asarum, and bai zhu in equal parts. Grind into a fine powder, take 2 qian each time, mix with warm wine after meals.

    Xiasin Powder for treating lung wind, cold nostrils, running clear nasal discharge, head pain, and chest discomfort.
    1 liang of asarum, roasted aconite (remove skin and navel), bai zhu, vitex fruit, pomegranate (wrapped and stewed, remove the pit), chuanxiong, and cassia heart each 7.5 qian; roasted zhiqiao and half a liang of honey fried licorice. Grind together (oral), take 3 qian each time, boil in 1 cup of water, add half a fen of fresh ginger, simmer until reduced to 6 fen, strain, and take after meals.[60p]
    Tongcao Pills (from "Ben Shi")
    Treats nasal congestion and clear nasal discharge caused by cold in the brain.
    Ingredients: Equal parts of Tongcao and Xinyi (each half of a liang), and one liang each of Xi Xin, Gan Sui, peeled Gui Xin, Chuan Xiong, and Fu Zi. Grind into a fine powder, mix with honey to form pills, wrap in cotton, and place in the nose, sealing tightly to prevent air from escaping. The pills should be slightly larger than millet. A slight sensation of pain is expected, indicating effectiveness.

    Xinyi Powder (from "San Yin")
    Treats nasal congestion, coolness in the brain, and persistent clear nasal discharge.
    Ingredients: Each of Xi Xin, Chuan Jiao, Gan Jiang, Chuan Xiong, Wu Zhu Yu, Xinyi, and Fu Zi, 7.5 qian; half a liang of soapwort shavings; one liang of Gui Xin; and six liang of pig fat. First, simmer the pig fat to create a grease, soak the first eight ingredients in bitter wine, then incorporate them into the oil. Cook Fu Zi until yellow, then use cotton to pack the mixture into the nose.

    Xi Xin Ointment (from "Qian Jin")
    Treats nasal congestion, cold in the brain, and persistent clear nasal discharge.
    Ingredients: Each of Xi Xin, Chuan Xiong, Chuan Jiao, black Fu Zi (gunpowdered, with skin and navel removed), Gan Ge, and Wu Zhu Yu, 2.5 qian; 3.3 qian of Gui Xin; and 1.65 qian of soapwort shavings. Use two liang of pig fat to prepare oil; soak the herbs overnight in rice vinegar, then add them to the pig fat and simmer until Fu Zi is yellow. Apply the mixture with cotton to fill the nose.[61p]
    Nasal Plug Ointment: Treats persistent clear nasal discharge.
    Ingredients: Cinnamon heart, Chuan xiong, roasted dried ginger, and Sichuan pepper each half a tael; 2.5 qian of soap pod. Fry until it sweats, then grind into a fine powder. Mix with sheep fat to form an ointment. Use a piece the size of a jujube seed, wrap in cotton, and insert into the nose.

    White Atractylodes Pill: Treats continuous clear nasal discharge.
    Ingredients: Grind white atractylodes into a fine powder. Mash green onion white, mix to form small pills the size of a mung bean. Take twenty pills, wash down with tea or broth, at any time.

    Fangfeng Decoction: Treats heat traveling to the brain from the gallbladder, resulting in nasal congestion and continuous thick discharge, akin to a gushing spring, which if prolonged, can lead to nosebleeds.
    Ingredients: 1.5 taels of fangfeng without reed, one tael each of huang qin, ginseng, roasted licorice, chuan xiong, and mai men dong (discard the heart). Grind into a fine powder. Take two qian with hot boiled water after meals, three times a day.

    Cang'er San: Treats continuous thick nasal discharge, known as nasal congestion.
    Ingredients: 0.5 taels of xin yi, 2.5 qian of fried cang'er seed, one tael of white fragrant atractylodes, and 0.5 taels of mint leaves. Grind into a fine powder. Take two qian with green onion tea after meals.[62p]
    Yin San: Treats lung heat, nasal congestion with thick mucus.
    Ingredients: Xixin, Baizhi, Fangfeng, Qianghuo, Danggui (root), Banxia, Chuanxiong, Jiegeng, Chenpi, and Fuling, each in equal parts – ten ingredients total, ground together. Make into a paste, add three qian of mint, and boil with ginger for consumption.

    Nanxing Decoction: Treats wind pathogen entering the brain, lingering cold not dispelled, hard obstructions in the nose causing blockage, and unexpressed brain qi, resulting in runny mucus. Use top-grade white nanxing (not limited in quantity), slice it, rinse with boiling water twice, and dry. Each dose is two qian, boiled with seven dates and a bit of licorice, taken after meals. After three to four doses, the obstruction will dislodge, brain qi will circulate, and the mucus will subside. Also use garlic and Piper cubeba powder, make into a cake, heat with gauze, apply to the forehead, and use a hot iron to warm through. Optionally, utilize 香附 and Piper cubeba powder sprinkled into the nose.

    Xinyuan Pills: Treats head wind, with nasal discharge resembling white lead.
    Ingredients: Nanxing prepared with ginger, Banxia prepared with ginger, Cangzhu soaked in rice wash, Xinyuan, Huangqin stir-fried in wine, Chuanxiong, Huangbo stir-fried until charred, Talcum ground, Oyster calcined, each in equal parts to make fine powder, shaped into pills, taken with mint tea.

    Chuanxiong Pills: Treats foul-smelling brain diarrhea.
    Ingredients: Use two liang of raw Chuanxiong, half a liang each of raw Cangzhu and Cao Wu (skin and tip removed). Grind into fine powder, mix with flour into pills, the size of tung seeds, taking ten pills after meals with clear tea. After taking the medicine, avoid hot substances temporarily.[63p]
    Sheep Lung Powder: Treats nasal discharge and brain leaks.
    One sheep lung, four ounces of white atractylodes, one ounce each of epimedium, mutong, dried ginger, and chuanxiong. Grind these five ingredients into a fine powder. Adjust the consistency with water to a suitable thickness, then administer into the lungs. Cook until done, dry it out, and grind into a fine powder. After eating, take two qian with rice wine.

    Xixin Powder: Treats nasal polyps and loss of sense of smell.
    Equal parts of northern xixin and gourd seeds, ground into a powder. Wrap like bean-sized pellets and insert into the nostrils. Also called Gourd Seed Powder.

    Nasal Hemorrhoid Remedy:
    Two qian each of bitter clove and sweet-succory, and two and a half fen each of indigo, blue cohosh tips, and dried white alum. Grind into a fine powder, mix with sesame oil to a hard consistency, not soft. Roll into balls the size of nostrils and insert into the nose, pressing against the polyp. Use once daily.
    Another remedy for blocked nasal passages and obstructed breathing, due to meat pillars: if not removed, healing is impossible. Other medicines may lead to temporary benefits but will result in regrowth; this remedy should be used.
    Twenty earth gallbladders and one white dog gallbladder. First, grind the earth gallbladders into a powder and place inside the dog gallbladder, tying it securely for three days. Then, during sunrise, have the patient lie with their head facing west and nostrils towards the sun. An assistant should use a quill to apply the medicine into the nostrils, once a day. After five or six days, there might be pain near the eyes in the nostrils, indicating the need to release. Wait another three or four days to apply again. Gradually, sneezing will occur, and it will fall out; dispose of it in a place where it won’t be obstructed. After it falls, immediately plug the nostril with cotton and avoid wind exposure.[64p]
    Formula for Treating Nasal Polyps

    Ingredients:

    • Gansui (a herb)
    • Red Cinnabar
    • Realgar (a mineral)
    • Orpiment (a mineral)
    • Rhizoma Veratri (a plant)
    • Alum (calcined)
    • Gourd stalk (all equal parts)

    Preparation: Grind the above ingredients into a powder and mix with honey to apply to the nose.

    Xinyigao (Magnolia Oil) Treats nasal polyps that cause obstruction and occasional pain.

    Ingredients:

    • Three taels of Magnolia leaves
    • Xuanshin (a plant)
    • Muxiang (a plant)
    • Baizhi (Angelica dahurica)
    • Blanched almond (remove skin and tip), each half tael

    Method: Use two taels of sheep marrow and pig lard, blend with the above medicines in a stone vessel, and simmer over low heat until it becomes a paste, turning red-yellow. Let it cool, then add one qian (a measure) of dragon brain and musk, shape into pills, and place in the nose wrapped in cotton. It will fall off within a few days, and the condition will be cured.

    Qing Huang San (Light Yellow Powder) Treats nasal polyps.

    Ingredients:

    • Half a tael of Realgar
    • Light powder (Talc)
    • Blanched almond (remove skin and tip), each one qian
    • A small amount of musk

    Method: Grind the four ingredients in a clean mortar, first turning the almonds into a paste, then adding Realgar, light powder, and musk, and grind to a very fine consistency. Seal in a small box. For patients, regardless of distance, apply a grain-sized amount on the nasal polyps every other night for half a month to observe results.[65p]
    Er Ding San: Treats the inability to smell, nasal discharge, and similar symptoms. Ingredients: Seven pieces each of bitter clove, clove, and red adzuki bean. Grind into a fine powder and blow into the nose using a bamboo tube. Also treats migraines. One variation includes seven pieces of corn and a small amount of gypsum.

    Nasal Polyp Formula:
    Ingredients: One tael of alum, seven castor beans, five pieces of salted plum meat, and a little musk. Pound into balls, wrap in cotton, and insert into the nose to contact the polyp, waiting for it to dissolve and clear water to flow out, with the polyp falling away.

    Di Long San: Treats nasal polyps.
    Ingredients: Earthworm (cleaned and fried) 2.5 qian, one pig's tooth soap pod. Calcine and grind to a powder. First, clean the nose, apply honey inside, place a small amount of the medicine, and let the clear water flow out until the polyp is eliminated.

    Wu Xi Wan: Treats nasal ulcers.
    Ingredients: One tael of powdered black rhinoceros horn, one tael of powdered antelope horn, powdered cow bile, and each one tael of cleaned bupleurum, powdered powdered realgar, roasted tian dong (without heart), roasted fritillaria (without heart), half a tael of huanglian, and half a tael of ginseng; all processed to the same weight of 7.5 qian of zhi mu, two and a half qian each of huang qin and roasted licorice. Grind together finely, mix well, and form into pills the size of a walnut. Take twenty pills with warm wine, on an empty stomach.[66p]
    Sheng Di Huang Decoction: Treats sores in the nose, with persistent itching and pain.
    Use equal parts Sheng Di juice and ginger juice, one liang of Ku Shen, three he of lard, and two qian of salt flower. Soak the Ku Shen in Sheng Di juice and ginger juice overnight, then mix with lard in a copper or stone vessel. Simmer nine times up and down until the juice is absorbed by the lard, then strain and pour into a box. Apply a small amount to the sores. It is also effective for various wind-heat sores. Add the salt flower halfway through.

    Chun Gen Decoction: Treats sore mouths and noses caused by malnutrition.
    Peel and slice Chun Gen, one sheng; finely chop half a sheng of scallion whites; add half a he of salt and stir-fry one he of prickly ash until fragrant. Combine with half a sheng of fermented soybeans. Mix with three sheng each of vinegar and clear wash water, boil for several dozens of rounds, strain to yield about one sheng, and divide into three doses. It works immediately if there are adverse substances expelled. Adjust dosage for children according to size.

    Wu Xiang Powder: Treats nasal sores that erode the nasal structure.
    Charred grass root ash and musk in equal parts, ground very finely; apply a small amount to the sore.

    Xi Jiao Powder: Treats lung heat, heart distress, and dry nose without discharge.
    Ingredients: Xi Jiao, Mu Tong, Sheng Ma, Chi Fu Ling, Huang Qi, Ma Ya Xiao, peeled bitter almonds, roasted until yellow, all half a liang; Mai Dong without the heart, one liang; ground vermilion; ground dragon brain; roasted licorice, each two qian and five fen. Grind all ingredients into a fine powder. Take one qian after meals, mixing it with bamboo leaf decoction for ingestion.[67p]
    Sanggen Baipi Powder: Treats accumulation of heat in the lungs, dry skin, nasal pain without discharge, headache, and chest tightness. Ingredients: Sanggen Baipi, Mutong, Da Huang (processed), each 120 grams, Shigao, Gegen each 180 grams, Shengma 75 grams, and roasted Gan Cao 30 grams. Grind into a powder; take 9 grams each time, decoct with one cup of water until reduced to 120 ml, and take warm after meals.

    Nasal Spray: Treats dryness and lack of nasal discharge. Ingredients: 1.5 grams of Longnao, 3 grams of Mayanxiao, and 14 Gua Ti seeds. Grind very finely; use a pea-sized amount and blow into the nose.

    Baizhi Powder: Treats cold wind entering the lungs, causing nasal congestion and pain. Ingredients: Baizhi soaked in apricot kernel soup, skin and tips removed, 3 grams of Xixin, 2 roasted scorpions. Grind to a fine powder and mix with sesame oil for application.

    Myrrh Powder: Treats the above conditions. Ingredients: Myrrh without oil, dried scorpions without soil, roasted; Nanshing hue, Bai Fuzhi processed; Xionghuang ground; Danggui roasted; Dansha ground; Huhuanglian; and Niu Huang ground; Baizhi; and musk ground, each 7.5 grams; U She (snake) soaked in wine, skin and bones removed, roasted, 15 grams. Grind into a fine powder, mix well; take 1.5 grams each time with warm wine, morning and evening.[68p]
    Bai Xian Pi Decoction treats lung ailments caused by wind, resulting in a pale complexion, occasional redness of the cheeks, dry skin, and nasal congestion with dryness and pain—this is classified as deficiency wind. Ingredients include Bai Xian Pi, Mai Dong (without heart), Bai Fu Ling (peeled), Xi Xin (without sprouts), and sweet almonds (peeled with tips removed) all in equal parts of one and a half liang, as well as Sang Bai Pi and Shi Gao (ground) each in two liang. For each dose, take three qian, boil with three cups of water and three he of soybeans, extract one cup of the broth, remove the beans, add the herbs and simmer until reduced to seven parts, strain, and take at any time.

    Hu Lu Wine is used for nasal congestion, blurry vision, pain, and brain fog. Take a sufficient amount of bitter Hu Lu seeds, crush them, and immerse them in half a sheng of good wine, letting it steep for three days in spring, one day in summer, five days in autumn, and seven days in winter; then, inhale a little through the nose. There’s also a method using children's urine to soak the juice.

    Shen Xia Xuan Nao San treats yellow discharge from the nose. Ingredients include Chuan Yu Jin, Chuan Qiong, Qing Dai, Bo He, and Xiao Huang each two fen, ground into a fine powder. For use, take a small amount and hold it in the mouth with cold water, then snuff it up the nose.

    Sheng Ma Fang Feng San treats a red nose. The ingredients are Sheng Ma, Fang Feng, and Ren Shen each one liang, half a liang of dry scorpions (stir-fried), two qian of xiong huang, one qian of niu huang, two and a half qian each of gan cao and zhu sha, one qian of musk, half a liang of dried silkworms (stir-fried). Grind these into a fine powder, combine with honey to form pills the size of cherries, coated in zhu sha. Each dose consists of one pill taken with bo he decoction.[69p]
    Gui Ziren Wan: Treats lung heat and red nasal discharge. Use any amount of Gui Ziren, grind into fine powder, and form into pills the size of a tung seed. Take twenty pills after meals with tea or wine.

    Bai Fan San: Treats lung wind, alcohol-related nasal congestion, etc. Use equal parts of Bai Fan, sulfur, and frankincense, grind into powder. Use fingers to gently press on the affected area, applying the medicine.

    Liu Huang San: Treats alcohol-related nasal congestion and black comedones on the nose. Use one qian each of sulfur and light powder, along with twenty-seven blanched apricot kernels. Grind into fine powder, mix with saliva, and apply to the nose before sleeping; wash off in the morning.

    Ling Xiao Hua San: Treats alcohol-related nasal congestion. Use equal parts of Ling Xiao Hua and mountain gardenia, grind into fine powder. Take two qian after meals with tea.

    He Shou Wu Wan: Treats lung wind, red nose, and red face. Use one and a half liang of He Shou Wu, one liang each of Fang Feng, peeled black beans, and Jing Jie spikes, as well as one liang each of cleaned Di Gu Pi, and half liang each of Sang Bai Pi, Tian Xian Teng, Ku Shen, and red earth. Grind into fine powder, mix with honey to form pills the size of a walnut. Take thirty to forty pills after meals with clear tea. One formulation includes one liang of dried root.[70p]
    Da Feng You: Treats lung wind, facial redness and nasal redness.

    Ingredients:

    • Seven pieces of Cao Wu
    • Fifty wen of Da Feng You
    • Fifty wen of genuine musk

    Preparation: Grind Cao Wu into a fine powder, mix it with musk, then add Da Feng You and stir well in a ceramic container over heat. First, rub the affected area with fresh ginger, then apply the medicine, two to three times a day. Also, take He Shou Wu pills to address the underlying issue.

    Lung Wind and Nasal Redness Formula[71p]
    Seven pieces of Aconite, half a cash of alum, a word of musk, and one cash of pig's tooth soap pod; these are to be ground into a fine powder. Mix with camphor oil and melt over a ceramic fire. First, rub with ginger, then use a finger dipped in the medicine to apply it, three times a day.

    For a nasal condition from alcohol use:
    Three cash of raw sulfur, one and a half cash each of Sichuan goldthread, white alum, and frankincense, and half a cash of light powder; these should be ground fine and applied with saliva, two times a day. Another formula treats the alcoholic nasal condition, excess flesh on the nose, freckles, and can also treat moles.

    Five wen of yellow lead, thirty wen of realgar, ground very fine, ten dried beans (shelled), the paper stopper should be oil-free, and fifty wen of medicinal cakes, placed in a jar. Mix everything in the medicinal cake jar and simmer over slow heat until boiling a couple of times. Remove from heat and then add three cash of finely ground raw mineral ash and chicken egg white, mixing well. Use a goose feather to wipe the red area of a red nose, once a day. The medicine will expel toxins, and once the ailment recedes, stop using it. Afterward, take dispersing powders such as birch bark powder. For freckles, use a small bamboo stick to apply the medicine to the affected areas; as soon as swelling appears, wash it off. If not washed, the medicine may be too strong.

    Another formula for treating a red nose and facial sores:
    Fifty wen of camphor oil, one Aconite in powder, one hundred wen each of light powder and musk; first, mix the Aconite into the oil and simmer until well combined. After a while, add the light powder and musk powder and stir well. Use a small amount to apply to the area until warm, and it will heal in ten days. If there is no light powder, rub the area with raw ginger to apply the medicine.[72p]
    Song for Treating Nasal Redness Due to Lung Wind

    Lung wind and nasal redness are hard to treat; I have a good remedy for you. Just use finely powdered alum, mixed with tomato juice, and apply it to see remarkable results.

    Jingjie's Powder - for treating lung wind and nasal congestion.
    Jingjie spikes - 4 taels, Fangfeng, peeled apricot kernels - 1 tael, fried white silkworms, fried thistle (spines removed) - 1 tael each, and roasted licorice - 1 tael. Grind these into a fine powder, and take 2 qian after meals with warm tea.

    Castor Oil Ointment - for treating alcohol-induced nasal redness and lung wind causing facial sores.
    Remove the shells from castor beans, grind them, and grind together with light powder, pitch, sulfur, and yellow wax - each 2 qian. Add 1 liang of sesame oil; boil into an ointment, and store in ceramic. Apply a small amount to the affected areas.

    Lead Red Powder - for when wind-heat attacks the Yangming meridians, resulting in purple-red spots and itchy rashes on the face and nose, commonly known as lung wind, as it is superficially present in the skin.
    Use half a liang of overseas sulfur and white alum ash, ground into powder, add a little yellow lead powder to match the patient’s facial color, apply half a qian, dampen with saliva, and reapply after brushing teeth or before bed. Also, take a Shengma decoction with Qing pills to eliminate the root cause.

    Jingjie Lianqiao Decoction [from Returning to Life] - for nasal congestion.
    Jingjie, Chaihu, Chuanxiong, Danggui, Shengdi Huang, Chi Shao, Baizhi, Fangfeng, Bohe leaves, Zhizi seeds, Huangqin, and Jiegeng, each 5 fen; Licorice - 3 fen. Grind and make into one pack, decoct with water for drinking.[73p]

      Treats phlegm from heat cough in summer, with a red face and irritability, and clear nasal discharge.
      Ingredients: Huangqin, Zhimucao, Sangbaipi, Xingren, Shanzhi, Tianhuafen, Beimujiao, Jiegeng, Licorice — equal parts.
      Use two sheng of water, decoct to eight parts, take on an empty stomach.

    Fangfeng Tongsheng San from Hejian
    Treats wind-heat attacking upwards, nasal congestion, and related symptoms.
    Ingredients: Fangfeng, Chuanxiong, Danggui, Chishao, Mahuang, Lianqiao, Boheye, Dahuang, Mangxiao — each five qian; Shigao, Huangqin, Jiegeng — each one liang; Huashi three liang; Licorice two liang; Jingjie, Baizhu, Zhiziji — each two qian five fen.
    Grind this into a powder, take two qian, steep in one large sheng of water with three slices of ginger, decoct to six or seven parts, and take warm. The "Yijian" adds wine-fried Huanglian and Boheye, named Huanglian Tongsheng San, for treating nasal discharge syndrome.

    Xiaofeng San (from "Jufang")
    Treats wind-heat attacking upwards, with headache and dizziness, heavy nasal congestion, and itching from rashes.
    Ingredients: Jingjie Flower, Fried Licorice, Ren-shen, Chuanxiong, Fangfeng, Qianghuo, Bohe, Jiaotong (fried cicada slough), Jiangcan (fried silkworm), Fuling — each two qian; Chenpi, Houpu — each two qian.
    Grind this into a powder, take two to three qian, mix with clear tea to serve.[79p]
    Nasal Redness Treatment
    Powder 7 parts of light powder, 1 part each of alum, mercury, and Beijing ink, and 49 pieces each of apricot, large fengzi, and schisandra, and 7 pieces each of walnut and white poplar leaves. Grind all into a powder and mix with egg white to apply to the affected area.

    Shen Yu Powder
    Treats lung heat, nasal discharge, and blockage. Equal parts of fine xing, white peony, wind protection, qianghuo, angelica, processed pinellia, chuanxiong, platycodon, dried tangerine peel, and poria. Grind into a powder. Take 3 qian with a decoction of mint and ginger.

    Wind Protection Powder
    Treats the above symptoms.
    One liang each of wind protection without reed, wood unblocker, and mai dong without heart, one liang of chuan shengma, taxillus, and kudzu; 7.5 qian of honey-fried licorice, 2 liang of gypsum. Grind into a powder. Take 5 qian with a large cup of water, decoct down to 5 parts, strain, and take warm without regard to time.

    Xiao Chai Hu Decoction (Zhongjing)
    Treats the above symptoms.
    500 grams of chaihu, ½ sheng of pinellia, 3 liang each of ginseng, huang qin, fresh ginger, and licorice, 12 jujubes split open. Combine these 7 ingredients with 12 sheng of water, boil down to 6 sheng, strain and re-boil to extract 3 sheng, take 1 sheng warm, 3 times a day.[80p]
    Shengma Ge Gen Decoction: For treating earlier symptoms.
    Shengma, Ge Gen, Shaoyao, and Gancao in equal parts, decocted in water. Take when cold for more heat, and when hot for more cold.

    Shen Su Decoction [from "Jufang"]: For treating seasonal colds with wind and cold, symptoms include heavy voice and nasal congestion.
    Ren Shen, Zi Su Ye, Gan Ge, Qian Hu, Chen Pi, Zhi Ke, Ban Xia, Fu Ling each 8 fen; Mu Xiang, Jie Geng, Gancao each 5 fen; water 2 sheng, 5 slices of ginger, 1 jujube, decoct until 8 parts remain, take warm.

    Xiao Feng Bai Jie Powder [from "Jufang"]: For treating seasonal cold damage with headache, fever, and cough from wind and cold, symptoms include heavy voice and nasal congestion.
    Jing Jie Sui, Ma Huang, Bai Zhi, Cang Zhu, Chen Pi each 1 qian; Gancao 5 fen; add water 1 sheng, decoct with ginger and scallions until 8 parts remain, take warm. If cough is severe, add 1 Wu Mei.

    Loquat Leaf Pills [from "Zheng Zong", same below]: For treating the initial stage of nasal allergy with redness, if prolonged, leads to blisters and swelling.
    Loquat leaves (with hairs and spines removed) 8 liang, Huang Qin stir-fried in wine 4 liang, flower powder 4 liang, Gancao 1 liang, all ground into a powder, mixed with new Anjiu to form pills the size of a tongzi; each dose is 1 qian 5 fen, taken after meals and before sleep, can be swallowed with hot water or tea. Avoid stir-frying with strong wine.[81p]
    Huangqin Qingle Decoction: Treats the same symptoms as before.
    Ingredients: Chuanxiong, Danggui, Chishao, Fangfeng, Shengdi, Tianhuafen, Gande, Lianqiao, Honghua each 1 qian; Huangqin 2 qian; Bohe 5 fen; water 2 zhong. Boil down to 8 fen, take after meals with a cup of wine.

    Zhenjun Miaotie Powder: Treats red and swollen nasal passages.
    Ingredients: 10 jin of pure sulfur powder, 5 jin each of buckwheat flour and white flour. Mix with a little clean water to achieve a suitable consistency, spread in a wooden box to form thin sheets, wrap in paper, dry in the wind, and store. Grind finely before use, and mix with fresh well water for application.

    Qishou Huoxiang Decoction: Treats prolonged nasal discharge of yellow and turbid mucus, leading to dizziness.
    Ingredients: 5 qian of Huoxiang with branches and leaves; water 1 bowl, boil down to 7 fen, add one boar's gallbladder, mix well, and take after meals. Do not exceed three doses for severe cases. If the bitterness is intolerable, use 1 liang of Huoxiang powder, boil down the boar's gallbladder into a thick paste and form into pills, with each dose being 2 qian taken with hot water after meals.

    Qinghua Decoction (from Jingyue Quanshu): Treats brain leaks.
    Ingredients: 2 qian each of Paeonia and Mai Dong; 1 qian of Dendrobium; 2-3 qian each of Danpi, Fuling, Huangqin, and Shengdi; water 1 zhong, boil down to 7 fen, take warm after meals.[82p]

    Acupuncture

    The "Ling Shu" says: What causes a person to sneeze? Qi Bo replies: It is the harmonious yang qi, full in the heart, that exits through the nose, which causes sneezing. To nourish the vital essence of the yang at the eyebrows, it is also said to be above the eyebrows. The "Jia Yi Jing" states: When pathogens invade the channels of the foot yangming, they cause nasal discharge and cold in the upper teeth. For this, pierce the area at the junction of the nail of the middle toe and its flesh, one on each side, taking from the left to treat the right, and from the right to treat the left.

    For headaches, body heat, nasal blockage, labored breathing, restlessness, fullness, and lack of sweating, this is treated by Quche. For heavy pain in the head and neck that causes stiffness and nasal obstruction with nasal bleeding, and breathing issues that cannot be relieved, Tongtian is the treatment. For headaches caused by wind, discomfort when exposed to wind or cold, nasal bleeding, and breathing difficulties, Chengling is indicated.

    For neck pain preventing looking back, excessive tearing, increased eye discharge (eye fatigue), nasal bleeding, redness and pain in the corner of the eyes, qi obstruction, unclear hearing and vision, throat tension affecting the neck, and muscle cramps that do not ease, Fengchi should be used. For headaches caused by wind, a blocked nose, sneezing, and running clear nasal fluids, Fengmen is the point of treatment. For wind-related headaches, nasal bleeding, frequent sneezing, and migraines, Zhuanzhu is indicated.

    For shoulder and back pain, nasal bleeding, difficulty breathing, and an inability to discern scents, Tianyou should be used. In cases of febrile illness with nasal blockage, Lieque is the primary point.[91p]

    • For excessive sleeping, with pain in the nasal cartilage and nasal discharge, treat with the two interstices.
    • For nasal discharge and bleeding, when there is a fever and sweating cannot occur, with a feeling of fullness in the chest and difficulty breathing, treat with Yangxi.
    • For heaviness in the head and nasal bleeding, treat with Zhiyin.
    • For nasal discharge and bleeding, with soreness and heaviness in the waist, spine, and feet, treat with Chengshan.
    • For fever where sweating does not occur, nasal bleeding, aversion to wind, and nasal obstruction, treat with Luyue. For deficient malarial fever and nasal bleeding, treat with Feiyang.
    • In cases of mania with excessive speech, but in truth involving nasal discharge and bleeding, treat with Pianli.
    • For nasal obstruction, treat with Qianggu.
    • For persistent nasal discharge and bleeding, use the foot taiyang. If there's bleeding from Dazhi and Xuè blood, treat with hand taiyang; if it continues, needle below the wrist bone; if it persists, needle the middle of the knee for bleeding.
    • For nasal blockage, needle the left if the left is blocked and the right if the right is blocked. For pain below both ribs with discharge above and below, fullness in the chest and shortness of breath, and when sweating cannot occur, nourish the hand taiyang to relieve it.
    • For nasal discharge and bleeding, treat with Shangxing; first needle Yanhxi, then Tianyou and Fengchi.
    • If there is a sore in the nasal canal causing illness, treat with Naokong.[92p]
      Nasal obstruction has no benefit, causing blockage of airways, excessive nasal discharge, and potential pus formation. For these symptoms, "Yingxiang" is indicated. If blood is present in the discharge, and there are hanging abscesses, with the passage blocked and unable to distinguish scents, "Heliao" should be used.

    If there is a nasal obstruction with clear discharge that cannot be stopped and blood is present, also pointing to possible pus, "Heliao" is appropriate.

    For internal nasal polyps causing nasal obstruction, headaches in the forehead and temples, or ulcerations within the nose, "Duanjiao" is indicated.

    If there is nasal obstruction preventing breathing, inability to gather mucus, not distinguishing between scents, along with persistent nosebleeds, "Shuigou" is used. If the bleeding does not stop, "Chengjiang" and "Weizhong" are suggested.

    The "Zishengfang" states that when there is excessive nasal discharge, moxibustion on "Yanhui," "Qianting," and "Yingxiang" is advisable.

    The "Medical Outline" notes that for clear and cloudy nasal discharge, moxibustion on "Shangxing" (two to seven times) will clear the excess and replenish the deficiency.

    Another method suggests targeting "Shangxing," "Renzhong," and "Fengfu"; if there is no improvement, proceed with "Baihui," "Fengchi," "Fengmen," and "Dazhu."

    For turbid nasal discharge: moxibustion on "Shangxing," "Quchi," and pricking "Hegu." If still ineffective, target "Renzhong" and "Yingxiang."

    For nasal polyps or bleeding: focus on "Fengchi," "Fengmen," "Fengfu," "Renzhong," and "Heliao."

    For nasal blockage with inability to smell: creating a point at "Yingxiang" and pricking upward slightly, while avoiding moxibustion. Use "Shangxing" for three points.

    Another method: target "Yingxiang," "Shangxing," and "Hegu"; if there is no resolution, moxibustion on "Renzhong," "Fengfu," and "Baila."[93p]
    Acupuncture for nasal congestion specifically targets the foot Taiyang meridian. According to the texts, the foot Taiyang is also known as Feiyang, located seven inches away from the ankle, and branches off to the Shaoyin. This is actually for treating nasal blockage and head pain, which is the main purpose of this technique.

    The "Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment" states: For moxibustion, the Yuhui point is directly above the nose, two inches into the hairline, about the size of a bean is the acupuncture point, to be moxibustion seven times. Additionally, at the Tongtian point, one inch on either side of Yuhui, moxibustion seven times. If there is foul odor in the left nostril, moxibustion on the left; if in the right, moxibustion on the right, applying the same treatment on both sides. I have used this method on several patients, and all had foul odor removed from the nose like decaying bones—unbearable smell, and their conditions were completely cured.

    The "Orthodox Surgical Texts" details a secret method for treating nasal hemorrhoids. First, use fennel powder and blow into the nostrils twice. Then, take two fine copper chopsticks with a small hole drilled in one end, threading a silk string through. Maintain a gap of about five minutes between the ends of the chopsticks, inserting the ends directly onto the root of the nasal hemorrhoid. Twist the string tightly and pull down; the hemorrhoid will naturally come off. Place it in water to observe its size, and use powdered fetal hair and ivory mixed to blow into the nostrils; this will stop the bleeding. Avoid spicy foods.

    The "Complete Works of Jingyue" states that moxibustion at the Yuhui point seven times treats nasal issues and hemorrhoids.

    For treating thick nasal discharge, apply moxibustion at the Shangxing point three times or seven times, and at the Tongtian point seven times; after moxibustion, nasal discharge will be expelled, leading to recovery.

    For treating nasal obstruction and excessive mucus, apply moxibustion at Yingxiang, Renzhong, Dazhui, Hegu, Fengfu, Quchai, Baihui, and Fengchi; for foul nasal discharge, apply moxibustion three times and, if not effective, seven times.[94p]
    Guidance

    The "Traditional and Contemporary Medical Systems" states: Sit facing east, without interruption, performing three channels; use the hands to pinch both nostrils, treating nasal ailments. Cross the legs and sit; this also treats nasal issues. Sit with legs extended to treat nasal sores, clearing the mucus, ensuring the nasal passages are open to perceive scents. With prolonged practice, one can fully appreciate fragrances from all directions.

    Another method: Sit with the knees together and feet apart, without interruption, performing five channels to treat nasal sores.

    Additionally: Sit upright and stretch the waist, slowly inhaling through the nose, using the right hand to pinch the nose, gradually closing the eyes and exhaling to remove nasal polyps.

    The "Book of Nurturing Life" states: Wipe the nose to moisten the lungs, consistently using the index finger on both sides of the nose bridge, wiping twenty to thirty times, warming both inside and out, known as irrigating Mount Zhongyue to nourish the lungs.

    Furthermore, regularly remove nasal hair, as it is said to be the gateway for spirit energy in and out.[95p]
    The "Secrets of Preserving Life" states: For nasal issues that prevent one from smelling scents or odors, use a method of guidance. With the tip of the middle finger and the palm, rub and heat the acupoints for "迎香" (Yingxiang), and you may also incorporate movement of the breath as you do this.

    For the breathing technique, return to the origin, focus on cleansing the life gate, imagine the kidney water rising up to Kunlun and descending to the navel. Then, from the left breast, push along the meridian down to "涌泉" (Yongquan), inhale and exhale there, and also direct your breath to the affected areas in the nose while shaking the tailbone. If the affliction is on the left side, push from the right nostril to the left "涌泉" afterwards, and visualize cleansing the navel and kidneys, imagining water flooding the crown and returning to the navel. If you experience redness in the cheeks or nose, disperse the redness, allowing the kidney water to wash the lungs, and over time it will subside.

    For nasal congestion from wind, first clear the lung meridian by rubbing the sides of the nose with both hands to warm both inside and outside. If excess heat rises, fix your gaze on the soles of your feet while meditating.[96p]
    Medical Case

    In "Records of Uncommon Oddities," it is said: Duke Di Liang was skilled in medicine, particularly in acupuncture. During the Xianqing period, he entered the borders as commanded, traveling through Huazhou, where the streets were filled with crowds. People gathered like a wall. Duke Di Liang pulled back the reins and observed from a distance a large board with big characters stating: "Whoever can cure this child shall be rewarded with a thousand bolts of silk." Upon closer inspection, he saw a wealthy family's child, about fourteen or fifteen years old, lying beneath the board with a growth at the tip of his nose, as large as a fist, its base attached to the nose like the stem of food, causing severe pain when touched. His eyes were almost closed by the growth, the whites of his eyes showing as he writhed in agony, close to death. Compassionately pondering for some time, he then said: "I can treat this." The child's parents and relatives bowed their heads in prayer, promptly offering a thousand bolts of silk set beside him. The Duke ordered them to help the child sit up, then inserted a needle about an inch behind the head, asking the patient: "Has the needle's energy reached the afflicted area?" The patient nodded. The Duke swiftly withdrew the needle and the growth fell off easily, instantly restoring the child's eyes to their original state without pain. The parents and family, weeping and bowing in gratitude, offered him silk as a gift. The Duke smiled and said: "I grieve for the severity of your situation; I am merely a physician responding hastily to a dire need. I am not a performer of tricks." He disregarded their offerings and left.

    In "The Confucian Family and Respecting Parents," it is stated: Chang Zhongming often, during hot weather, exposed his skin to seek coolness, and was taken by the wind. He suffered nasal congestion for three days, despite sitting in a warm place, and was not relieved. A person recommended the use of Tongsheng Powder, which he cooked with fresh ginger, scallion roots, and fermented soybeans. After three servings, he sweated profusely, and his nose was immediately unblocked.[97p]
    The "Danxi Heart Method" states: When a person has a runny nose with turbid mucus, foul odor, a thin and wiry pulse, a slippery right cun pulse, and a weak left cun pulse, first perform moxibustion at the Shangxing, Sanli, and Hegu points. Then use 2 taels of wine and Qian, 1 tael each of Cangzhu and Banxia, and 5 qian each of Xin Yi, Xi Xin, Chuan Xiong, Bai Zhi, Shi Gao, Ren Shen, and Ge Gen. Grind the herbs and divide them into seven doses for consumption to achieve complete recovery.

    The "Medical Outline" states: For the treatment of a man whose right nasal passage is running turbid mucus with foul odor, presenting a thin and wiry pulse, a slippery right cun pulse, and a weak left cun pulse, perform moxibustion at the Shangxing, Sanli, and Hegu points. Then use 2 taels of wine and Qian, and 1 tael each of Cangzhu and Banxia, as well as 5 qian each of Xin Yi, Xi Xin, Chuan Xiong, Bai Zhi, Shi Gao, Ren Shen, and Ge Gen. Divide into seven doses for consumption to achieve complete recovery. This is indicative of damp-heat phlegm accumulation.

    Sun Yikui said: I once treated a person using Fangfeng Tongsheng San to eliminate yellow bile, reducing the amounts of Talcum and Gypsum by half and doubling the quantity of Xin Yi flower. First, take three to five doses, and then use this to form pills, taking seventy pills each time, swallowed with warm water in the morning and evening. A total of half a jin will lead to recovery.

    The "Xue Ji Medical Case" states: A scholar who was diligent and suffered from wind-cold had a runny nose causing clear mucus, with cold restraining his sneezing. I said: This is due to spleen and lung qi deficiency, which cannot effectively regulate the pores. He did not believe it. After taking medicine to dispel wind, he felt numbness and fatigue in his limbs, and phlegm flowed freely, resembling a stroke. I said: This was caused by the wind remedies depleting the original qi; thus, the yin fire took over its soil position. Therefore, I supplemented the middle and replenished qi with Mai Dong and Wu Wei, treating him until recovery.[98p]
    In Honglu, Su Longxi suffered from coughing, shortness of breath, nasal congestion, and a runny nose. I prescribed a dose of Shen Su Decoction to disperse the cold pathogens, and also used Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction to reinforce the skin’s protective barrier, leading to recovery. Later, due to overexertion and anger, he experienced a recurrence. I used the previous decoction with additional Huang Lian and Zhi Shi; he had abdominal distension, lack of appetite, and reduced urination. I prescribed Er Chen and Si Ling, but the previous symptoms intensified, and urination became difficult. I said, “Abdominal distension and lack of appetite indicate a deficiency in the spleen and stomach; reduced urination indicates a deficiency in the lungs and kidneys; both are due to excessive attack.” I prescribed Liu Jun Zi, adding Huang Qi, Pao Jiang, and Wu Wei, and after two doses, all symptoms significantly diminished. I then used Bu Zhong Yi Qi with additional Pao Jiang and Wu Wei, and after several doses, he was completely cured.

    For Minister Wang from the Workshop, who suffered from wheezing, coughing, thirst, a red face, and a dry nose, I believed there was heat in the spleen and lungs. I used Er Chen Decoction with additional Qin, Lian, Shan Zhi, Jie Geng, and Mai Dong, resulting in recovery.

    For County Magistrate Ruan, who had a white face and a runny nose, this indicated a deficiency in the spleen and lungs coupled with an external pathogen. I used Bu Zhong Yi Qi with additional Fu Ling, Ban Xia, and Wu Wei, treating him until he recovered. Later, I used Liu Jun Zi and similar herbs for stabilization.

    A man who had a white face and a runny nose, unable to smell any scents—pleasant or unpleasant—for three years, was treated with Bu Zhong Yi Qi, adding Mai Dong and Shan Zhi, leading to recovery.[99p]
    A scholar, whenever he coughed, would use a remedy such as ginseng and perilla drink, and would recover. However, it recurred, and he used the same medication, resulting in a hoarse throat and a weak pulse on the left wrist. I assessed that the Yin fire of the kidney was harming and overcoming the lung metal, so I treated him with Liu Wei Di Huang Wan, adding Mai Dong, Wu Wei, and roasted Shan Zhi, along with Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang, and he recovered.

    In the first year of Wujing, when a person suffered from a cold with phlegm, he used medication to disperse the exterior and transform phlegm. With excessive phlegm causing coughing, his abdomen was distended, and his face was pale—indicative of a deficiency in the spleen that could not generate lung metal. I prescribed Liu Jun Zi Tang with added Jie Geng, and he immediately recovered. After three days, the previous symptoms reappeared, with a clear nasal discharge, indicating a recurrence of a cold. I used the previous medication, adding Sang Pi and Xing Ren, as well as Jie Geng, and he recovered.

    Zhong Suzi from Changzhou had an abscess on his nose, belonging to superficial pathogenic factors, but both his qi and blood were deficient, preventing the dispersal. So, I primarily used Bu Zhong Yi Qi, supporting it with Fang Feng and Bai Zhi, and he recovered.

    In "Zheng Zhi Zhun Sheng," it is said that Sun's aunt had not smelled any scents for many years. Later, due to another illness, her friend Miao Zhongchun prescribed a formula, using Sang Bai Pi in amounts of seven to eight qian; after taking it for some time, her nasal congestion unexpectedly resolved.

    In "Han Shi Yi Tong," it is recorded that a nobleman had a fleshy growth in his nose, emitting an unbearable odor and causing pain upon any movement, leaving him helpless. I simply used a bit of powdered alum mixed with a small amount of Nao Sha, blowing it into the nostrils, and shortly thereafter it transformed into water and disappeared. Along with this, I applied Sheng Shi Tang combined with Xie Bai San in two doses, and he was cured. This was due to thick flavors obstructing, with damp heat steaming at the lung entrance, akin to mushrooms suddenly sprouting after the rain clears.[100p]

    Original

    古今图书集成医部全录卷一百五十一

    鼻门 【鼻衄详载血门，此不复入】

    　　　　黄帝素问

    　　　　　金匮真言论

    　　西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻。
    　　【注　西方金位，白者金色。肺属金脏，鼻者肺之窍也。】　　春善病鼽衄。
    　　 【注　所谓善病者，言五脏之经俞在外，风伤肌腠，则易入于经也。鼽衄，头面之经证也。春气在头，故善病鼽衄也。】　　又曰：冬不按蹻，春不鼽衄。
    　　 【注　按蹺者，按摩导引，引阳气之通畅于四肢也。冬时阳气伏藏，若导引其四出，则无以奉春生之气，是以病鼽衄也。】
    　　　　　阴阳应象大论

    　　肺主鼻。
    　　 【注　肺气通于鼻，肺和则鼻能知香臭矣。故肺主开窍在鼻。】
    　　　　　五脏别论

    　　五气入鼻，藏于心肺。心肺有病而鼻为之不利也。　　【注　心肺居上为阳，肺乃心之盖而主气，开窍于鼻，故病则鼻不利也。】[1p]
    　　　　　热论

    　　伤寒二日，阳明受之。阳明主肉，其脉侠鼻络于目，故身热目疼而鼻干不得卧也。　　 【注　阳明之气主肌肉。身热者，病阳明之气也。病虽在气，而阳明之脉侠鼻络目而属胃，故有目疼鼻干之形证。胃不和，故不得卧也。】
    　　　　　刺热篇

    　　脾热病者鼻先赤。
    　　 【注　土位中央，故鼻先赤。】

    　　　　　缪刺篇

    　　邪客于足阳明之经，令人鼽衄。
    　　 【足阳明之脉起于鼻，邪客之，则令人鼽衄。】
    　　　　　气厥论

    　　胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊。鼻渊者，浊涕下不止也。传为衄。　　 【注　胆气上升，则热随入脑。侠鼻两旁曰頞。辛頞者，鼻頞辛酸也。鼻渊者，浊涕下不止也。盖脑为精髓之海，髓者骨之充也，脑者阴也，故脑渗则为涕。杨元如曰：肾主藏精而居下，脑为精髓之海而居上，胆者中精之府也。三者并主藏精，精气相通，故胆邪移入于脑也。热气上升，迫于络脉，则为衄。】[2p]
    　　　　　气交变大论

    　　岁木不及，复则咳而鼽。
    　　 【注　肺开窍于鼻，故咳而鼽。鼽者，鼻流清涕也。复为母郁而子复也。】　　岁金不及，民病鼽嚏。
    　　 【注　鼽嚏，肺病也。】

    　　　　　脉解篇

    　　阳明所谓客孙脉则头痛、鼻鼽、腹肿者，阳明并于上，上者则其孙络太阴也。故头痛、鼻鼽、腹肿也。　　 【注　阴阳之气上下升降，内外出入，行于脉外之气分也。气分者，皮肤肌腠之间。上谓皮肤之上也。夫诸脉之浮而常见者，皆络脉也。足太阴之脉，亦见于皮肤之上而无所隐，是以阳明之气并于上，则迫于阳明之孙络，与太阴之经脉也。迫于阳明之孙络则头痛鼻鼽，迫于太阴之经脉则腹肿也。】
    　　　　　至真要大论

    　　太阳司天，民病鼽衄。
    　　 【注　鼽衄，乃阳热中盛之病。】　　少阴之复，烦躁鼽嚏，甚则入肺，咳而鼻渊。　　少阴司天，客胜则鼽嚏。[3p]
    　　 【注　鼽嚏，厥阴之气胜也。】
    　　少阳司天，甚则鼽衄。

    　　　　　解精微论

    　　泣涕者脑也，脑者阴也，髓者骨之充也，故脑渗为涕。
    　　　　　五常政大论

    　　审平之纪，其脏肺，其主鼻。
    　　 【注　肺开窍于鼻也。】
    　　少阳司天，火气下临，肺气上从，咳嚏、鼽衄、鼻窒。　　 【注　上从者，因司天之气下临，畏其胜制而从之也。欬嚏、鼽衄、鼻窒，皆肺病也。】　　太阳司天，寒气下临，心气上从，鼽嚏善悲。　　 【注　寒气下临，则藏气上从也。火性炎上，水性润下。火气妄行于上，故霜寒以复之。鼽嚏善悲，火热铄金也。】　　少阴司天，热气下临，肺气上从，嚏鼽衄，鼻窒。　　阳明司天，初之气，民病鼽衄、嚏、欠、呕。　　 【注　鼽衄、嚏、欠、呕者，风木之气也。】　　少阳司天，三之气，民病鼽衄、嚏、欠。　　少阴司天，民病鼽衄，阳明所至为鼽嚏。　　热至则鼽衄。[4p]

    　　　　　刺法论

    　　帝曰：余闻五疫之至，皆相染易。天牝从来，复得其往。气出于脑，即不干邪。　　【注　天牝，鼻也。鼻受天之气，故曰天牝。】
    　　　　　邪气脏腑病形篇

    　　十二经脉三百六十五络，其血气皆上于面，而走空窍。其宗气上出于鼻而为臭。　　 【注　宗气者，胃腑所生之大气，积于胸中，上出于肺，以司呼吸，故出于鼻而为臭。】
    　　　　　本神篇

    　　肺藏气，气舍魄。肺气虚则鼻塞不利，少气，实则喘喝，胸盈仰息。　　 【注　肺主气以司呼吸，故肺气虚则鼻塞不利。】[5p]
    　　　　　经脉篇

    　　足太阳之别名曰飞扬，别走少阴，实则鼽窒头背痛，虚则鼽衄。　　大肠手阳明之脉，其支者上挟鼻孔。所生病者，目黄、口干、鼽衄。　　胃足阳明之脉起于鼻之交頞中，下循鼻外。所生病者鼽衄。　　 【注　凡此皆经脉所循之分而为病也。】
    　　　　　口问篇

    　　口鼻者，气之门户也。
    　　【注　夫口、鼻、耳、目皆为空窍，故曰口鼻者　气之门户也。】
    　　　　　师传篇

    　　鼻隧以长，以候大肠。鼻孔在外，膀胱漏泄。　　 【注　鼻乃肺之窍，大肠肺之腑，故鼻以候大肠。膀胱者津液之腑，气化则出，鼻孔在外，谓鼻孔之气出在外，则膀胱漏泄，盖上窍通而下窍泄也。】
    　　　　　五阅五使篇

    　　鼻者，肺之官也。肺病者，喘息鼻张。　　 【注　官之为言司也。阅其官之象，则可知其脏之有病矣。】[6p]
    　　　　　忧恚无言篇

    　　人之鼻洞涕出不收者，颃颡不开，分气失也。　　 【注　肝脉循喉咙入颃颡。颃颡者腭之上窍。口鼻之气及涕唾从此相通。故为分气之所泄，谓气之从此而分出于口鼻者也。人之鼻洞涕出不收者，因颃颡不开，分气失也。】
    　　　　　脉度篇

    　　肺气通于鼻，肺和则鼻能知香臭矣。
    　　　　扁鹊难经

    　　　　　鼻属肺其用属心

    　　四十难曰：肺主声，鼻者肺之候而反知香臭，其意何也？然。肺者西方金也，金生于巳，巳者南方火也，火者心，心主臭，故令鼻知香臭。　　 【注　肺，金也。声出于金，故肺主声。心，火也，火之化物，五臭出焉，故心主臭。肺主声，鼻属于肺，不能听声而反知香臭，果何如耶？盖由肺属金，金长生在巳，南方巳午未，巳正火临官之地，火在脏为心，心主臭，鼻虽属于肺，肺金生于心火之位，故令鼻知香臭。】[7p]
    　　　　金匮要略 【汉□张机】

    　　　　　鼻塞清涕

    　　肺痈，胸满胀，一身面目浮肿，鼻塞清涕出，不闻香臭酸辛，咳逆上气，喘鸣迫塞，葶苈大枣泻肺汤主之。
    　　　　　鼻燥

    　　酒黄疸者，或无热，静言了了，腹满欲吐，鼻燥。其脉浮者先吐之，沉弦者先下之。
    　　　　中藏经 【汉□华佗】

    　　　　　不闻香臭常流清涕

    　　肺风者，胸中气满，冒昧汗出，鼻不闻香臭，喘而不得卧者，可治。　　肺实则鼻流清涕。

    　　　　　死色

    　　肺死则鼻孔开而黑，黑色起于鼻上，渐入于口者死。黑白色入口鼻目中者，五日死。
    　　　　仁斋直指方 【宋□杨士瀛】

    　　　　　鼻齆

    　　鼻齆者，肺为风冷所伤，津液冷滞，鼻气不宣，香臭不知。宜芎藭散。
    　　　　济生方 【宋□严用和】[8p]

    　　　　　论治

    　　夫鼻者肺之候，职欲常和，和则吸引香臭矣。若七情内郁，六淫外伤，饮食劳役，致鼻气不得宣调，清道壅塞。其为病也：为衄，为痈，为瘜肉，为疮疡，为清涕，为窒塞不通，为浊脓，或不闻香臭。此皆肺脏不调，邪气蕴积于鼻，清道壅塞而然也。治之之法，寒则温之，热则清之，塞则通之，壅则散之，无越于斯。但时气鼻衄，不可遽止，如出三升以上，恐多者方可断之。《活人书》所谓衄血者乃解，盖阳气重故也。不可不知。　　鼻者肺之所主，职司清化，调适得宜，则肺脏宣畅，清道自利。摄养乖方，则清道壅塞，故鼻为之病焉。盖肺藏于气，肝藏于血，邪热伤之则血熟，血热则气亦热，血气俱热随气上逆，故为鼻衄，甚则生疮。风寒乘之，阳经不利，则为壅塞，或为清涕，蕴积不散，则不闻香臭，或为鼻齆，或生瘜肉鼻痛之患矣。又有热流胆腑，邪移于脑，遂致鼻渊。鼻渊者浊涕下不止也。传为衄蔑瞑目，故得之气厥也。[9p]
    　　　　疮疡全书 【金□窦汉卿】

    　　　　　瘜肉 【即鼻痔】

    　　鼻居面中，为一身之血运，而鼻孔为肺之窍，其气上通于脑，下行于肺。若肺气清，气血流通，百病不生。肺气盛，一有阻滞，诸病生焉。鼻孔中瘜肉名曰鼻痔，皆由六气七情所感而生。若生上入眼，名曰胬肉。若生下入鼻中，名曰瘜肉。窒塞不通，当戒酒节欲，除烦恼，戒忧愁。内服煎剂，外用点药，庶平复矣。[10p]
    　　　　河间六书 【金□刘完素】

    　　　　　焦干

    　　鼻孔燥干者，金肺之本，肺藏气，以血液内损，气虚或风，则皴揭。风能胜湿，热能耗液，皆能成燥。故经云，风热火兼为阳，寒湿燥同为阴。又燥湿亦异也。然燥金虽属秋阴，而其性异于寒湿，燥阴盛于风热火也，故风热甚而寒湿同于燥也。然中寒吐泻亡液而成燥者亦以此矣。故经云，诸濇枯涸，干劲皴揭，皆属于燥也。　　夫伤寒之候，头项痛，腰脊强，身体拘急，表热恶寒，不烦躁，无自汗，或头痛，肌热，鼻干，或胸满而喘，手足指末微厥，脉浮数而紧者，邪热在表，皆麻黄汤发汗之证也，或天水散之类甚佳。
    　　　　　鼻渊

    　　胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊，浊涕不止，如涌泉不渗而以下，久不已，衄血为患。防风汤主之。[11p]
    　　　　　鼻鼽

    　　鼽者鼻出清涕也。夫五行之理，微则当其本化，甚则兼乎鬼贼。故经曰：亢则害承乃制也。易曰：燥万物者莫熯乎火。以火炼金，热极而反化为水，及身热极则反汗出也。水体柔顺，而寒极则反冰如地也；土主湿阴云雨而安静，土湿过极则反为骤注烈风雨淫溃也。木主温和而生荣，风大则反凉而毁折也。金主清凉，秋凉极而万物反燥也。皆所谓过极则反兼鬼贼之化，制其甚也。由是肝热甚则出泣，心热甚则世汗，脾热甚则出涎，肺热甚则出涕，肾热甚则出唾也。经曰：鼻热者出浊涕。凡痰涎涕唾稠浊者，火热极甚，销铄致之然也。或言鼽为肺寒者误也。彼但见鼽嚏鼻窒，冒寒则甚，遂以为然，岂知寒伤皮毛，则腠理闭密，热极怫郁，而病愈甚也。　　小腹膀胱，按之内痛，若沃以汤。濇于小便，上为清涕。太阳直行从巅入络于脑，气下灌于鼻，时出清涕不止也。[12p]
    　　　　　鼻窒

    　　鼻窒，窒、塞也。火主(月真)膹肿胀，故热客阳明而鼻中(月真)胀则窒塞也。或谓寒主闭藏，妄于鼻窒为寒者，误也。盖阳气盛于上而侧卧，则上窍通利，而下窍闭塞者，谓阳明之脉左右相交，而左脉注于右窍，右脉注于左窍。故风热郁结，病偏于左，则右窍反塞之也。俗不知阳明之脉，左右相交，注于鼻孔。但见侧卧则上窍通利，下窍窒塞，反疑为寒尔。所以否之道者，象其肺金之盈缩也。[13p]
    　　　　　病色

    　　脾风鼻黄，脾热鼻赤。

    　　　　　嚏

    　　嚏，鼻中因痒而气喷作于声也。鼻为肺窍，痒为火化，心火邪热干于阳明，发于鼻而痒则嚏也。或故以物扰之痒而嚏者，扰痒属火故也。或视日而嚏者，由目为五脏神华，太阳真火，日光耀于目，则心神躁乱而发热于上，则鼻中痒而嚏也。伤寒病再经衰而或嚏者，由火热已退而虚热为痒，痒发鼻则嚏也。或风热上攻，头鼻壅滞，脉浮而无他证者，内药鼻中得嚏，则壅滞开通而愈也。或有痛处因嚏而其痛不可忍者，因嚏之气攻冲结痛，而不得通利故也。[14p]
    　　　　东垣十书 【元□李杲】

    　　　　　肺和则知香臭

    　　金匮真言论云：西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻，藏精于肺。夫十二经脉三百六十五络，其气血皆上走于面而走空窍，其精阳气上走于目而为睛，其别气走于耳而为听，其宗气出于鼻而为臭。《难经》云：肺气通于鼻，肺和则能知香臭矣。夫阳气宗气者，皆胃中生发之气也，其名虽异，其理则一。若因饥饱劳役损脾胃，生发之气既弱，其营运之气不能上升，邪塞孔窍，故鼻不利而不闻香臭也。宜养胃气，使阳气宗气上升鼻管则通矣。又一说，《难经》云：心主五臭，肺主气，鼻者肺窍反闻香臭者，何也？盖以窍言之肺也，以用言之心也。因卫气失守，寒邪客于头面，鼻亦受之不能为用，是不闻香臭矣。故经曰，心肺有病，鼻为之不利。洁古曰：视听明而清凉，香臭辨而温暖者是也。治法宜先散寒邪，后补卫气，使心肺之气得交通，则鼻利而闻香臭矣。丽泽通气汤主之。[15p]
    　　　　　流清涕

    　　冬三月阴气在外，阳气内藏，当外助阳气，不得发汗，内消阴火，勿令泄泻，此闭藏周密之大要也。盛冬乃水旺之时，水旺则金旺，子能令母实。肺者肾之母，皮毛之元阳本虚弱，更以冬月助其令，故病者善嚏，鼻流清涕，寒甚出浊涕，嚏不止，比常人大恶风寒，小便数而欠，或引行小便色清而多，大便不调，夜寒无寐，甚则为痰咳、为呕、为秽、为吐、为唾白沫，以至口开目瞪，气不交通欲绝者，吴茱萸丸主之。[16p]
    　　　　　窒塞

    　　肺藏贼邪，燥热相合，鼻窒、鼽衄、血溢、血泄。其脉濇而浮大甚者，桃仁承气汤；微者，犀角地黄汤；极者，抵当汤，微极抵当丸。　　鼻为肺之窍，因心肺上病而不利也。有寒有热，是皆伤于皮毛，气不利而壅塞，壅塞清道气不利，宜通。寒则表之，麻黄、桂枝之类；热则清之，芩、连、栀子之类。
    　　　　　体属肺用属心

    　　经云：五气入鼻，藏于心肺。《难经》云：肺主鼻，鼻和则知香臭。洁古云：视听明而清凉，香臭辨而温暖，此内受天之气而外利于九窍也。夫三焦之窍，开于喉，出于鼻。鼻乃肺之窍，此体也；其闻香臭者，用也。心主五臭，舍于鼻，盖九窍之用皆禀长生为近，心长生在酉，酉者肺，故知鼻为心之所用而闻香臭也。故肺有病而鼻为之不利也。此明为清气所奉于天，而心劳胃损，则受邪也。[17p]
    　　　　丹溪心法 【元□朱震亨】

    　　　　　酒齄

    　　酒齄鼻是血热入肺，宜用四物汤加陈皮、红花、酒炒黄芩，煎入好酒数慨，就调炒五灵脂末同服。《格致论》中于上药有茯苓、生姜，气弱者加黄芪。　　酒齄者，此皆壅热所致。夫肺气通于鼻，清气出入之道路，或因饮酒，气血壅滞，上焦生热，邪热之气留伏不散，则为之鼻疮矣。又有肺风，不能饮而自生者，非尽因酒耳。宜一味淅二泔，食后用冷饮。外用硫黄入大菜头内煨研涂之。若鼻尖微赤及鼻中生疮者，辛夷研末，入脑、麝少许，绵裹纳之；或以批杷叶拭去毛，銼，煎汤，候冷调消风散，食后服。[18p]
    　　　　格致余论 【元□朱震亨】

    　　　　　面鼻得冷则黑

    　　诸阳聚于头，则面为阳中之阳，鼻居面中央，而阳明起于頞中，一身之血运到面鼻，到面鼻阳部，皆为至清至精之血矣。酒性善行而喜升，大热而有峻急之毒。多酒之人，酒气熏蒸，面鼻得酒血为极热，热血得冷，为阴气所搏，汗浊凝结，滞而不行，宜其先为紫而后为黑色也。须用融化滞血，使之得流，滋生新血，可以运化，病乃可愈。予为酒制四物汤加炒片芩、茯苓、陈皮、生甘草、酒红花、生姜，煎调五灵脂末饮之；气弱者加酒黄芪，无有不应者。[19p]
    　　　　古今医统 【明□徐春甫】

    　　　　　病属于肺

    　　经曰：鼻者肺之外候。又曰：西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻。又曰：鼻热甚，出浊涕。又曰：心肺有病而鼻为之不利是也。按《巢氏病源》曰：肺开窍于鼻，热乘于血，则气亦热也。血气俱热，血随气发出于鼻为鼻衄，甚则大衄而口耳皆出血也。又云：肺脏调和，则鼻气通利而知香臭。若邪乘太阴，其气蕴积于鼻者，则津液壅塞，鼻气不得宣调，故不知香臭而为齆也。至于生疮变成瘜肉，或窒塞，或流涕，皆是肺经之邪壅滞也。[20p]
    　　　　　病属于火

    　　鼻中痒而气喷，作于声为嚏。夫痒为火化，心火邪热干阳明，发于鼻则痒而嚏也。有以物扰之而嚏，有视日而嚏者，盖太阳真火耀于目而扰于心，则火热冲上，鼻中痒而嚏也。有风热上攻，头鼻壅塞，有因嚏而痛者，虽证候之不同，同为热也。凡为病不同，邪热所乘之经无有异也。鼻窒与嚏痒者，热客阳明胃之经也。鼽涕者，热客太阴肺之经也。盖鼻者足阳明胃经所主，阳明脉左右相交，注于鼻孔。又鼻者肺之窍，故肺气通于鼻，其邪热干于二经，发于鼻而为窒塞鼽涕之证。故经曰：心肺有病，而鼻为之不利也。[21p]
    　　　　　鼻鼽瘜肉皆邪气结成

    　　肺气通于鼻，清气出入之道。肺脏热邪壅滞，上焦郁结，伏留不散，而成齆瘜之患矣。
    　　　　　鼻赤酒齄血热入肺

    　　酒齄鼻多是饮酒之人。酒气邪热熏蒸面鼻，血热壅滞而成鼻齄，赤色者也。或有肺经素有风热，虽不因酒，亦自红黑而生齄也。
    　　　　　鼻窍不利治宜辛散苦泻

    　　心肺有热而鼻为之不利也。或外伤风寒，内热愈窒，壅塞不闻。或流清涕或痒而嚏者，宜麻黄、桂枝、细辛、辛夷之辛味以散。不因外感而惟内热者，宜芩、连、栀子之苦味以泻之。二法为治鼻之大纲也。
    　　　　　鼻疮

    　　鼻热生疮色红，内无壅塞，此为血热。宜用生地黄、四物汤加酒制片芩、酒拌红花、生甘草、麦门冬、天门冬之类。
    　　　　　鼻渊

    　　经曰：胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊。刘河间用防风通圣散加薄荷、黄连各二钱，水煎服。[22p]
    　　　　　鼻酸

    　　鼻酸乃痰火所为，宜凉膈散加荆芥穗、桔梗之类。
    　　　　　鼻痒

    　　鼻痒乃热则生风故也，宜防风通圣散加白附子、僵蚕之类。
    　　　　　食入脑中

    　　卒食物从鼻中缩入脑中，介介痛不出，牛脂膏甚良。
    　　　　医学正传 【明□虞抟】

    　　　　　鼻证

    　　《内经》曰：西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻。又曰：鼻者肺之外候。丹溪曰：肺之为脏，其位高，其体脆，性恶寒又恶热。是故好饮热酒者始则伤于肺脏，郁热久则见于外而为鼻齄、准赤之候。得热愈红，得寒则黑，此谓热极，是水之象，亢则害承乃制也。其或触冒风寒，始则伤于皮毛，而成鼻塞不通之候。或为浊涕，或流清汁，久而不已，名曰鼻渊，此为外寒束内热之证也。《原病式》曰：肺热则出涕是也。又有胆移热于脑则为辛頞鼻渊，鼻中浊涕如涌泉不渗而下，久而不已，则为鼻蔑衄血、塞肉鼻齆等证。各以类推而治之。[23p]
    　　　　　脉法

    　　右寸脉浮洪而数，为鼻衄鼻齄。
    　　左寸脉浮缓，为伤风鼻塞，鼻流清涕。
    　　　　　鼻为元牝之门

    　　老子曰：谷神不死，是为元牝。元牝之门，为天地根。绵绵若存，用之不勤。何谓元牝之门？答曰：鼻通天气曰元门，口通地气曰牝户。曰鼻乃元牝之门户也。
    　　　　证治要诀 【明□戴思恭】

    　　　　　流涕

    　　鼻塞流涕不止，有冷热不同。清涕者，脑冷肺寒所致，宜细辛、乌附、干姜之属。浊涕者，乃《素问》所谓胆移热于脑，则为鼻渊是也。宜防风、甘菊之属，须以清浊别冷热。　　有不因伤冷而涕多清，或黄或白，或时带血如脑髓状，此由肾虚所生，不可过用凉剂，宜补脑散，仍以黑锡丹、紫灵丹、灵砂丹。　　伤冷热，鼻暴塞，流涕多者，通关散。[24p]
    　　　　　色诊

    　　余处无恙，独鼻尖色青黄者，此其人必为淋也；鼻尖微白者，亡血也；赤者血热也。
    　　　　医学入门 【明□李梴】

    　　　　　窒塞

    　　鼻窍于肺，而能知香臭者心也。人身水升火降，荣卫调和，则鼻司呼吸往来不息而已。苟或寒伤皮毛则鼻塞不利，火郁清道则香臭不知。新者偶感风寒，鼻塞声重流涕喷嚏，宜以风寒治之，加味羌活汤、参苏饮、消风百解散。久则略感风寒，鼻塞等证便发，乃肺伏火邪，郁甚则喜热恶寒，故略感冒而内火便发，宜清金降火兼通气之剂，凉膈散加荆芥、白芷，或川连石膏散。又有不必外感，四时鼻塞干燥，不闻香臭，宜清金降火消痰之药，清气化痰丸，上清丸。古方鼻塞甚者，御寒汤、澄茄丸；不知香臭者，通气汤；内有硬物者，单南星饮贴顖，荜茇饼外用，石菖蒲、皂角等分为末，绵包塞鼻，仰卧片时；虚寒者通草丸。[25p]
    　　　　　鼻鼽

    　　鼻乃清气出入之道。清气者胃中生发之气也。鼻塞久则气壅不转，热郁于脑，清浊混乱，为鼽、为衄、为渊。鼽者，鼻流清涕，热微，二陈汤加芎、归、细辛、白芷、防风、羌活、桔梗等分，姜煎，入薄荷少许。久不止者，芷夷散去薄荷加荆芥、黄芩、神曲、半夏、南星等分，食后煎服，外用细辛膏。[26p]
    　　　　　鼻渊

    　　渊者，鼻流浊涕，热盛，金沸草散倍黄芩，入凤凰壳一枚，烧存性，调服。肺风，消风散加发灰。肺火流涕，咳吐脓血，桔梗汤、人参平肺散。胆移热于脑，流涕浊臭，防风通圣散加薄荷、黄连，或芷夷散，外用苍耳茎苗子烧灰，酢调涂鼻内。鼻渊久则成衄，防风散主之。
    　　　　　脑砂

    　　有流臭黄水者，甚则脑亦作痛，俗名脑砂。有虫食脑中，用丝瓜藤近根五尺，烧存性为末，酒调服。虚者川乌散，外用白牛尾毛、橙叶等分为末，吹鼻中；倘有血出，加山栀亦不妨。
    　　　　　鼻齄

    　　鼻齄，准头红也，甚则紫黑。因饮酒血热入肺，复被风寒，郁久则血凝浊而色赤。或不饮者，乃肺风血热，俱宜四物二陈汤，去半夏加红花、黄芩，水煎，入酒少许，调五灵脂末服。气虚加黄芪，常宜服单山栀丸或黄连阿胶丸，间用升麻和气饮、吞泻青丸以除病根，外用黄连末，天钓藤烧灰，桐油调敷，或硫粉散。[27p]
    　　　　　鼻痛

    　　鼻痛因风邪入鼻，与正气相抟，鼻道不通，故痛。藿香正气散、袪风通气散。有痰火冲肺者，鼻隔隐痛，二陈汤加黄芩、山栀、桔梗、麦门冬。
    　　　　　鼻疮

    　　鼻疮，轻为鼻疮，重为鼻痔，皆肺热也。鼻中生疮者，枇杷叶煎汤，候冷，调消风散，食后服。忌煎炒姜蒜热物。外用辛夷为末，入脑、麝少许，绵裹塞鼻。
    　　　　　鼻痔

    　　鼻痔肺气热极，日久凝浊，结成瘜肉如枣，滞塞鼻窍。甚者又名鼻齆。宜防风通圣散，加三棱、海藻末调服。外用辛夷为君，细辛、杏仁少许为末，和羊髓、猪脂熬膏，候冷入雄黄、白矾、轻粉，麝香少许，为丸绵裹塞鼻，数日即脱。甚者加硇砂少许，或瓜矾散亦妙。又食积热痰生痔，单苍耳丸内服外敷，最消食积，或用白矾二钱，细辛一钱，白芷五分为末塞鼻。　　治法[28p]
    　　鼻证，大抵疏风降火为要法。风寒外感者，温以散之。风热有自内郁者，或外感久则郁而为热，或内因饮食衣服过暖，肝热生风，亦鼻塞流涕，宜降火清金。　　久则宜养血补肾为要。凡鼻涕鼽渊鼽，久甚不愈者，非心血亏则肾水少。养血则血生而火自降，补肾则水升而金自清。虽鼻疮痔虽久亦宜。又鼻塞久不愈者，必内伤肺胃，清气不能上升，非外感也。宜补中益气汤以和之。此皆治本之论。
    　　　　本草纲目 【明□李时珍】

    　　　　　病因

    　　鼻渊流浊涕，是脑受风热。
    　　鼻鼽流清涕，是脑受风寒，包热在内。　　脑崩臭秽，是下虚。
    　　鼻窒，是阳明湿热生瘜肉。
    　　鼻齄，是阳明风热及血热，或脏中有虫。　　鼻痛，是阳明热。[29p]

    　　　　医学纲目 【明□楼英】

    　　　　　鼻塞

    　　鼻塞皆属肺。经云：肺气通于鼻，肺和则鼻能知香臭矣。又云：五气入鼻，藏于心肺。心肺有病，而鼻为之不利也。又云：西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻，藏精于肺。又云：肺主臭，在脏为肺，在窍为鼻是也。
    　　　　　鼻渊

    　　运气，鼻渊皆属热。经云：少阴之复，甚则入肺，咳而鼻渊，治以苦寒是也。
    　　　　　鼻鼽

    　　运气鼻鼽有二：一曰火攻，肺虚鼻鼽。经云：少阴司天，热气下临，肺气上从，鼽衄鼻窒。又云：少阴司天，热淫所胜，民病鼽衄，嚏呕。又云：少阳司天，火淫所胜，甚则鼽衄。又云：少阳之复，烦躁鼽嚏。又云：少阴司天，客胜则鼽嚏。又云：岁金不及，炎火乃行，民病鼽嚏。又云：金不及曰从革，从革之纪，其病嚏咳鼽衄，治以诸寒是也。二曰金助，肺实鼻鼽。经曰：阳明所至为鼽嚏，治以温剂是也。[30p]
    　　　　明医杂着 【明□王纶】

    　　　　　闭塞

    　　鼻塞不闻香臭，或但遇寒月多塞，或略感风寒便塞，不时举发者，世俗皆以为肺寒，而用表解通利辛温之药不效，殊不知此是肺经有火，邪火郁甚，则喜得热而恶见寒，故遇寒便塞，遇感便发也。治法清肺降火为主，而佐以通气之剂。若如常鼻塞不闻香臭者，再审其平素，只作肺热治之，清金泻火清痰，或丸药噙化，或末药轻调，缓服久服，无不效矣。此予所亲见而治验者。其平素原无鼻塞旧证，一时偶感风寒而致窒塞声重，或流清涕者，自作风寒治。　　【注　前证若因饥饱劳役所伤，脾胃发生之气不能上升，邪害空窍，故不利而不闻香臭者，宜养脾胃，使阳气上行，则鼻通矣。按东垣云：胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊，治之以防风汤。大抵胃气不和之所致者多矣。】[31p]
    　　　　奇效良方 【明□方贤】

    　　　　　论证

    　　鼻者肺之通窍，主清气出入之道路。若气血和平，阴阳升降，则呼吸通和，荣卫行焉，鼻和则知香臭矣。或六淫七情，内外伤感，又因饮食劳倦，因而鼻气不得宣通，清道壅塞。其为病也，若积热客于阳明，遂以迫血妄行，自鼻孔中出，谓之衄。热则津液中干，冷则脑髓流注，或风冷随气入于经，上贯于脑，下注于鼻，则涕下不能自收谓之流涕。或冷滞气塞鼻则不闻香臭，于是为鼻齆。血脉聚日久，缠绵转加壅结，变生瘜肉。或气壅滞于上为邪热留伏不散则为鼻疮，久则变为疳(上匿下虫)腐溃汁臭。鼻之为病，不过风热而已。[32p]
    河间云：鼻窒塞也，火主(月真)膹肿胀，故热客阳明而鼻中(月真)胀，则鼻窒塞也。或谓寒主闭藏，妄以鼻窒为寒者误也。盖阳气甚于上，而侧卧则上窍通利而下窍闭塞者，谓阳明之脉左右相交，而左脉注于右窍，右脉注于左窍，故风热郁结，病偏于左则右窍反塞之类也。所谓鼽者，鼻出清涕也。夫五行之理，微则当其本化，甚则兼其鬼贼，故经曰：亢则害承乃制也。易曰：燥万物者莫熯乎火。以火炼金热极而反为水，及其热极则反汗出也。由是肝热甚则出泣，心热甚则出汗，脾热甚则出涎，肺热甚则出涕，肾热甚则出唾。经曰：鼻热甚出浊涕。又云：胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊者，浊涕出不止也。凡痰涎涕唾稠浊者，火热甚销铄致之然也。[33p]
    或言鼽为肺寒者误也；但见鼽涕鼻窒，冒寒则甚，遂以为然。岂知寒伤皮毛，则腠理闭密，热气怫郁而痛愈甚也。及失嚏者，鼻中因痒而气喷作于声也。鼻为肺窍，痒为火化，心火邪热干于阳明，发于鼻而痒则嚏也。或故以物扰之痒而嚏者，扰痒属血。或故视日而嚏者，由目为五脏精华，太阳真火晃耀于目，则心神躁乱而发热于上，则鼻中痒而嚏也。或伤寒病衰而或嚏者，由火热已退而虚热为痒，痒发鼻则嚏也。或风热上攻，头鼻壅滞，脉浮而无他证者，内药鼻中得嚏，则壅滞开通而愈也。或有痛处因嚏而痛不可忍者，因嚏之气攻冲结痛而不得通利故也。三者之证，同为热也。故为病不同，邪热所乘之经有异故也。[34p]
    鼻窒与嚏痒者，热客阳明胃之经也。鼽涕者，热客太阴肺之经也。盖鼻者足阳明胃经所主，阳明之脉左右相交注于鼻孔。又鼻者肺之窍，故肺气通于鼻，其邪热干于二经，发于鼻而为窒塞鼽涕之证，故经曰：心肺有病而鼻为之不利也。治法观邪所中之何经治之，则不失矣。或因外冒风寒而痛转甚，遂作寒治而用温热之剂表散者，偶尔获中，岂知寒复于热，热郁浊气，清道不利，故有是证。或用辛甘发散，腠理开通，结滞得散，阳热外泄，微者则已，甚者郁结不开，其病转加者，虽用退热疏风辛凉之剂解之，即使结散热退，暂愈而已，全在乎验其内外结热之微甚，宜以辛温凉平之药可也。凡此诸证，全在医之识病治之，了然无不瘥矣。[35p]
    　　　　医学准绳六要【明□张三锡】

    　　　　　总论

    　　肺开窍于鼻，世所共知也。然阳明之脉挟鼻络目，结于迎香，左之右，右之左，去鼻孔各开五分，是穴。风邪从面而来，则入阳明，脉道怫郁，气不通畅，故清涕时出，久变为浊。所谓外寒束内热，论极有理。须辛散之。方书多用升麻、葛根、白芷、葱白，乃阳明经药也。郁热既久，顿发不开，必加辛凉，酒枯芩、薄荷之类。至如酒客膏粱辛热炙煿太过，火邪炎上，孔窍壅塞，则为鼻渊。鼻中浊涕如涌泉，渐变鼻蔑、衄血、瘜肉、鼻痔等证。即《素问》所谓胆移热于脑之义。[36p]
    　　　　　窒塞不通

    　　鼻塞，时值寒月，必加麻黄、细辛于升麻葛根汤中，佐以枯芩、苏叶，多加甘，桔为舟楫，庶易成功。已经发散未得全开，脉洪有力，口干鼻燥者，君以辛凉清之，酒芩、栀子、薄荷之属。仍佐刑、防、升、芷，不可骤用寒凉法也。　　气虚之人，气弱不能上升，则鼻塞滞。所谓九窍不利肠胃之所生是也。多服补中益气汤自通，此乃屡验者。　　鼻壅气不通不闻香臭，通草散主之。　　痰火郁结于上焦胸中肓膜之上，上窍不通，则元门闭密而鼻不闻香臭，口不知味，或耳聋目昏。良由大气弱不能上冲，浊气得以擅权，是虚为本而痰火为标也。当用补中益气汤，加升柴诸风药引上行，兼用清上化痰开窍丸药，戒性慎口，久之自全。[37p]
    　　　　　渊瘜酒齄

    　　火郁上焦，气不通，抑遏成涕，《内经》所谓肺热则出涕是也。方书谓脑渗为涕，恐非。　　浊涕如渊，《内经》谓胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊。要皆阳明伏火所致。宜防风通圣散一两，加薄荷、黄连各二钱五分，水煎服。或本方硝黄、滑石、石膏减半，倍加辛夷。　　瘜肉必由上焦积热，郁塞已久而生。然有诸中，然后形诸外。必内服清火利膈药，二陈、凉膈加减，须断酒薄味。　　酒齄乃热血入面，为寒所拂。热血得寒，污浊凝滞而然。服前药，外用梧桐子取油，入黄连，以天钓藤烧灰，热敷之。[38p]
    　　　　证治准绳 【明□王肯堂】

    　　　　　所属经络

    　　鼻頞中，頞亦作齃。鼻山根也，俗呼鼻梁，属足阳明胃经、督脉之会。　　 【注　《素问》曰：胆移热于脑，则辛頞鼻渊，传为衄蔑、瞑目。注曰：足太阳膀胱脉起目内眦，上额交巅络脑，阳明脉起于鼻，交頞中，旁约太阳之脉。今脑热则足太阳逆与阳明之脉俱盛，薄于頞上，故頞辛鼻渊。頞辛者，鼻酸痛也。鼻渊者，浊涕下而不止如水泉也。热盛则阳络溢，阳络溢故衄，衄者鼻出血汁也，又谓之蔑。血出甚则阳明太阳脉衰，不能荣于目，故目瞑也。】　　鼻属手太阴肺经。
    　　 【注　《素问》曰：西方白色，入通于肺，开窍于鼻，然畏热。《灵枢》曰：肺病者喘息鼻张。又曰：肺虚则鼻塞不利，和则能知香臭矣。乔岳曰：肺绝则无涕，鼻孔黑燥，肝逆乘之而色青。东垣曰：伤风鼻中气出粗，合口不开，气通于天也。】　　又属手少阴心经。[39p]
    　　 【注　李东垣曰：鼻本主肺，而复能闻香臭者，鼻中有心，庚金生于巳也。《素问》曰：五气入鼻，藏于心肺，心肺有病而鼻为之不利也。】　　又属手足阳明大肠胃经、督脉之交会。　　 【注　刘河间曰：伤风寒于腠理而为鼻塞者，寒能收敛，阳气不通畅也。《素问》曰：伤寒二日，阳明受之。阳明主肉，其脉侠鼻，故鼻干不得卧。王海藏曰：石膏发汗，辛寒入手太阴经。仲景治伤寒阳明经证乃用之者，何也？盖胃脉行身之前，而胸为胃肺之室，邪热在阳明，则肺受火制，故用辛寒以清肺，所以号为白虎汤也。《素问》又曰：运气阳明所至为鼽嚏。注鼽，鼻窒也；嚏，喷嚏也。】　　其在小儿面部，谓之明堂。[40p]
    　　 【注　《灵枢》曰：脉见于气口，色见于明堂。明堂者鼻也。明堂广大者寿，小者殆，况加疾哉？按此语即相家贵隆准之说也，然须视其面部何如。愚尝见明堂虽小与面相称者，寿可八十，要不可执一论也。】　　属足太阴脾经。
    　　 【注《素问》曰：脾热病者，鼻先赤。】　　侠鼻孔两旁五分，名迎香穴，属手足阳明大肠胃经之会。　　直两目瞳子，名巨髎穴，属足阳明胃经阴蹺脉之会。耳鸣口不知谷味，气不快，四肢困倦，行步不正，发脱落，食不下，膝冷，阴汗带下，喉中介介，不得卧，口舌嗌干太息，头不可回顾，项筋紧急，脊强痛，头旋，眼黑，头痛，呵欠，嚏喷。温卫补血汤、人参汤、辛夷散、增损通圣散、辛夷汤、醍醐散、通关散、防风汤、排风散、荜澄茄丸，皆治鼻塞之剂，宜审表里寒热而用之。[41p]
    　　　　　鼻齆

    　　鼻塞久而成齆。盖由肺气注于鼻，上荣头面。若上焦壅滞，风寒客于头脑，则气不通；冷气停滞，搏于津液，脓涕结聚，则鼻不闻香臭，遂成齆也。内服芎藭散、山茱萸丸，外用赤龙散、通顶散、雄黄散、黄白散、通草散。孙一奎曰：大肠，肺之腑也；胃，五脏之所受气者也。经曰：九窍不利，肠胃之所生也。鼻主无形者。经曰：清气通于天。又曰：鼻主天气。设肠胃无痰火积热，则平常上升之气，皆清气也。[42p]
    纵火热主令之岁，何尝病耶？若肠胃素有痰火积热，则其平常上升之气，皆蕴而为浊矣。金职司降，喜清而恶浊，今受浊气熏蒸，凝聚既久，壅遏郁结，而为涎涕，至于痔珠瘜肉之类，皆由积久，燥火内燔，风寒外束，隧道壅遏，气血升降，被其妨碍，浇培弥厚，犹积土而成阜也，即非火热主令之岁，有不病者乎？治者无拘于运气之说可也。　　细辛散、本事通草丸、三因辛夷散、千金细辛膏、川椒散、塞鼻柱膏，皆温热之剂，真是脑冷者，乃可用。白芷丸，有外感者乃可服。[43p]
    　　　　　渊鼽诸证治法

    　　泣涕者脑也，故脑渗为涕，故得之气厥也。王太仆注云：脑液下渗，则为浊涕。涕下不止，如彼水泉，故曰鼻渊也。额谓鼻頞也。足太阳脉起于目内眦，上额交巅，上入络脑。足阳明脉起于鼻交頞中，旁约太阳之脉。今脑热则足太阳逆，与阳明之脉俱盛，薄于頞中，故鼻頞酸痛也。热盛则阳络溢，阳络溢则衄出血汗也。血出甚，阳明太阳脉衰，不能荣养于目，故目瞑。厥者气逆也，皆由气逆而得之，宜服防风汤。　　亦有痰气者，宜南星饮。[44p]
    　　头风，鼻涕下如白带，宜辛夷丸。
    　　久患鼻脓极臭者，以冷水调百草霜末服。　　肺虚而壅，鼻生瘜肉，不闻香臭，羊肺散，鼻疳蚀，椿根汤、乌香散、蓝靛傅令遍，日十度，夜四度，立瘥。　　鼻干无涕，犀角散、桑根白皮散、吹鼻散。　　鼻痛，气道壅塞故也，内服人参顺气散，外傅白芷散。风冷搏于肺脏，上攻于鼻，则令鼻痛，没药散。　　肺受风，面色枯白，颊时赤，皮肤干燥，鼻塞干痛，此为虚风，白藓皮汤。　　鼻塞、眼昏、疼痛、脑闷、壶卢酒。[45p]
    　　　　外科正宗 【明□陈实功】

    　　　　　酒齄

    　　齄鼻属脾，由血热郁滞不散，所谓有诸内必形诸外。宜真君妙贴散，加白附子敷之，内服枇杷叶丸、黄芩清肺饮。
    　　　　　鼻痔

    　　鼻痔者，由肺气不清，风湿郁滞而成。鼻内瘜肉，结如榴子，渐大下垂，闭塞孔窍，使气不得宣通。内服辛夷清肺饮，外以硇砂散逐日点之，渐化为水，乃愈。兼节饮食，断厚味，戒急暴，省嗜欲，愈后庶不再发。
    　　　　　脑漏

    　　一名鼻渊，总因风寒凝入脑户，与太阳湿热，交蒸乃成。其患鼻流浊涕，或流黄水，点点滴滴，长湿无干，久则头眩，虚运不止。治以藿香汤主之，天麻饼子调之亦可渐愈。如日久虚眩不已，内服补中益气汤，六味地黄丸相间服之，以滋化原，始愈。[46p]
    　　　　医方考 【明□吴昆】

    　　　　　鼻病方论

    　　鼻居五官之中，疾非美观也。记曰：尽饰之道，斯其行者远矣。故考五方以治鼻。　　鼻流浊涕不止者，名曰鼻渊。乃风热在脑，伤其脑气，脑气不固而液自渗泄也。苍耳散四味，皆辛凉之品，辛可以驱风，凉可以散热，其气轻清，可使透于巅顶，巅顶气清，则脑液自固，鼻渊可得而愈矣。　　鼻生瘜肉，气息不通，香臭莫辨者，辛夷散主之。夫鼻者气之窍，气清则鼻清，气热则鼻塞，热盛则塞甚，此瘜肉之所以生也。故治之宜清其气。是方也，辛夷、细辛、川芎、防风、槁本、升麻、白芷，皆轻清辛香之品也，可以清气，可以去热，可以疏邪，可以利窍。[47p]
    乃木通之性可使通中，甘草之缓可使泻热。　　鼻中瘜肉，用针微刺，令患人含水一口，后以瓜蒂散和麝香少许，用水数滴吹鼻内，出涎水则愈。此苦能涌泄也，能泻其实则瘜肉愈矣。　　阳虚脑寒鼻渊者，补脑散主之。人身之上，天之阳也，故六阳之气皆会于面。若阳气自虚，则阴气凑之，令人脑寒而流清涕。是方也，天雄辛热而上浮，辛热者太阳之象，故可以温脑而补阳虚。辛夷仁、苍耳茸，皆轻清澈脑之剂，可以佐天雄而透脑。　　鼻赤如榴者，大(石卜)散，酒调敷之。夫鼻者热也，所以赤者血也。大黄寒能泻热，(石卜)硝咸能败血。此证耽酒者有之，若不绝酒而徒用药，抱薪救火，何益于事？[48p]
    　　　　景岳全书 【明□张介宾】

    　　　　　论证

    　　鼻为肺窍，又曰元牝。乃宗气之道而实心肺之门户，故经曰：心肺有病而鼻为之不利也。然其经络所至专属阳明，自山根以上，则连太阳督脉，以通于脑，故此数经之病皆能及之。若其为病，则窒塞者谓之鼽。时流浊涕而或多臭气者，谓之鼻渊，又曰脑漏。或生瘜肉而阻塞气道者，谓之鼻齆。及有喷嚏、鼻衄、酒齄、赤鼻之类，各当辨而治之。然总之鼻病无他也，非风寒外感，则内火上炎耳。外感者治宜辛散，内热者治宜清凉，知斯二者，则治鼻大纲尽乎是矣。[49p]
    　　　　　论治

    　　鼻塞证有二：凡由风寒而鼻塞者，以寒闭腠理，则经络壅塞而多鼽嚏。此证多在太阳经，宜用辛散，解表自愈。如川芎散、神愈散及麻黄、紫苏、荆芥、葱白之类，皆可择用。　　若由火邪上炎而鼻塞者，单宜清火。火之微者，多近上焦，出自心肺。宜清化饮、黄芩知母汤之类主之。　　火之甚者，多出阳明，或微兼头痛。宜竹叶石膏汤、凉膈散之类主之。　　若风寒兼火者，即防风通圣散之类，亦可用。大都常塞者多火，暴塞者多风寒，当以此辨之。　　鼻涕多者多由于火，故曰肺热甚则鼻涕出。由此观之，则凡无故多泪及多口涎者，亦多属肝脾之火，皆其类耳。　　鼻渊证总由太阳督脉之火，甚者上连于脑，而津津不已，故又名为脑漏。此证多因酒醴肥甘，或久用热物，或火由寒郁，以致湿热上熏，津汁溶溢而下，离经腐败，有作臭者，有大臭不堪闻者，河间用防风通圣散一两，加薄荷、黄连各二钱以治之。古法有用苍耳散治之者。[50p]
    然以余之见，谓此炎上之火，而治兼辛散，有所不宜，故多不见效。莫若但清阴火而兼以滋阴，久之自宁。此即高者抑之之法。故常以清化饮加白蒺藜五钱或一两，苍耳子二三钱。若火之甚者，再以清凉等剂加减用之，每获全愈。或用宣明防风汤之类亦可。但此证一见，即宜节戒早治，久则甚难为力也。　　凡鼻渊脑漏，虽为热证，然流渗既久者，即火邪已去，流亦不止，以液道不能扃固也。故新病者多由于热，久病者未必尽为热证。此当审察治之，若执用寒凉，未免别生他病。[51p]
    其有漏泄既多，伤其髓海，则气虚于上，多见头脑隐痛，及眩运不宁等证，此非补阳不可，宜十全大补汤、补中益气汤之类主之。　　鼻齆瘜肉，阻塞清道，虽鼻为肺窍，而其壅塞为患者，乃经络肌肉之病。此实阳明热滞留结而然。故内治之法，宜以清火清气为主；外治之法，宜以黄白散及千金瘜肉方、雄黄散，或简易瘜肉方之类主之。　　酒齄赤鼻，多以好酒之人湿热乘肺熏蒸面鼻，血热而然；或以肺经素多风热，色为红黑而生齄疖者，亦有之。内宜凉血清火，外宜硫黄散、白矾散轻搽。[52p]
    　　　　石室秘录 【清□陈士铎】

    　　　　　肿痛由火

    　　鼻肿者，乃肺经火盛也，宜用甘桔汤则效。今用皂角末吹入，打清嚏数十即愈。盖鼻因气壅，今打嚏则壅塞之气尽开散，故不必清肺而鼻肿自消也。
    　　　　　鼻大

    　　有人鼻大如拳，疼痛欲死。此乃肺经之火热壅于鼻而不得泄，法当清其肺中之邪，去其鼻间之火可也。方用黄芩、麦冬、花粉、甘草各三钱，桔梗、天冬各五钱，紫菀二钱，百部、苏叶各一钱，水煎服，四剂自消。此方全在群入肺经以去其火邪，又何壅肿之不消耶？此奇病而以常法治之者也。[53p]
    　　　　　孔生红线

    　　鼻中生红线一条，长尺许，少动之则痛欲死，人以为饮酒之病也，而余以为不然，亦祟也。方用硼砂、冰片各一分，研为末，以人乳调之，轻轻点在红线中间，忽然如觉有人将病人打一拳一般，顷刻即消。奇绝之方也。盖硼砂亦是杀祟之物也。

    　　南星饮　治风邪入脑，宿冷不消，鼻内结硬物，窒塞，脑气不宣，遂流髓涕。　　上等大白南星不拘多少，切成片　右用沸汤荡两次，焙干，每服二钱，用枣七枚、甘草少许煎，食后服。三四服后，其硬物自出，脑气流转，髓涕自收。仍以大蒜、荜茇末杵作饼，用纱衬炙热，贴顖前，用熨斗火熨透。或香附末及荜茇末，吹入鼻中。
